{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:54","updatedTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:54","title":"Amazon is selling products emblazoned with a far-right, white nationalist meme","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-selling-merchandise-alt-far-right-meme-groyper-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60edba5861b8600019f16d00?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A man wears a red Make America Great Again hat and a &#34;Groyper&#34; meme shirt showing the white nationalist group&#39;s Pepe the Frog-inspired logo. He is surrounded by pro-Trump protesters waving America and Trump flags outside the US Capitol building.\" height=\"605\" width=\"807\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A Trump supporter wears a &#34;Groyper&#34; meme shirt outside the United States Capitol building on January 6, 2021, the day of the Capitol riot.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Evelyn Hockstein/For The Washington Post via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Amazon is selling three products promoting the far-right meme Groyper.</li>\n<li>Groyper, a spinoff of Pepe the Frog, is closely linked with the white nationalist Nicholas Fuentes.</li>\n<li>On Monday, Media Matters for America reported additional items that appear to have been removed.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.insider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Insider&#39;s homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Amazon is selling books and a sticker set promoting the far-right white nationalist meme Groyper.</p><p>Groyper, a toad-like derivative of Pepe the Frog that looks like a giant green amphibian with a wide smirking face resting on intertwined hands, has been linked to far-right activism, including the white nationalist internet personality Nick Fuentes, whose followers call themselves &#34;Groypers&#34; and the &#34;Groyper Army.&#34; </p><p>Amazon, which has a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-removes-qanon-conspiracy-theory-products-from-site-2021-1\">history</a> of selling products associated with white supremacist and <a href=\"https://www.mediamatters.org/maga-trolls/amazon-sold-products-touting-transphobic-and-anti-vax-term-has-its-origins-far-right\">far-right</a> conspiracy theories like the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-qanon-merchandise-products-shirt-item-facebook-ban-conspiracy-theory-2020-10\">QAnon movement</a>, is currently selling several items emblazoned with the Groyper meme. </p><p>The merchandise includes two books - entitled &#34;The Groyper And Frens Coloring Book&#34; and &#34;Who&#39;s that_groyper?&#34; - both of which were written by the same person and are marked as children&#39;s books. As <a href=\"https://www.mediamatters.org/amazon/amazon-selling-products-promoting-far-right-meme-associated-white-nationalist-group\">Media Matters for America</a>, a left-leaning nonprofit that tracks right-wing media, first reported on Monday, the two products&#39; descriptions say that they were &#34;Sold and shipped by Amazon.&#34; While this can sometimes mean that Amazon bought inventory to supply to customers, it also applies to books that are self-published via the e-commerce giant&#39;s publishing platform.</p><p><strong><strong style=\"background-color: #ffff00;\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60eda6eeca74780018ae90e9?format=jpeg\" alt=\"This is a picture of a Groyper book on Amazon.\" height=\"972\" width=\"1301\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Groyper-Frens-Coloring-Book/dp/B087FGV3VS/ref=sr_1_2?dchild=1&#38;keywords=groyper&#38;qid=1626187220&#38;sr=8-2\" target=\"_blank\">Screenshot/Amazon</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></strong></strong></p><p>In addition, Amazon is listing a sticker that features a mashed-up image of Groyper and the wrestler Hulk Hogan, who became an icon among Groypers after the celebrity shared that same meme in a <a href=\"https://slate.com/technology/2017/12/groyper-the-far-right-s-new-meme-is-a-more-racist-version-of-pepe-the-frog.html\">now-deleted 2017 tweet</a>. </p><p>Media Matters reported that Amazon was also selling three Groyper-themed T-shirts with the meme creature&#39;s face and the text &#34;Groyper&#34; and &#34;Groyper Army&#34; on them, and <a href=\"https://archive.is/ioG22#selection-1967.8-1967.38\">provided</a> <a href=\"https://archive.is/qrf4e\">screenshots</a> <a href=\"https://archive.is/R781S\">taken</a> on Thursday of the listed products.</p><p>Insider verified the existence of the three T-shirt items like &#34;Groyper Political Meme T-Shirt&#34; on Monday afternoon, but an Amazon search for those titles yielded no results as of Tuesday morning, suggesting Amazon may have removed them. </p><p>Although a Google query for &#34;Amazon groyper&#34; shows two of the shirts - <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Groyper-Army-Political-Meme-T-Shirt/dp/B081HDQRNW\">&#34;Groyper-Army-Political-Meme-T-Shirt&#34;</a> and <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Groyper-Easter-Comfy-Halloween-T-Shirt/dp/B07ZFHWTMK\">&#34;Groyper-Easter-Comfy-Halloween-T-Shirt&#34;</a> - as the first two search options, clicking those links yields Amazon error pages that read, &#34;SORRY we couldn&#39;t find that page.&#34;</p><p>Amazon did not respond to a request for comment.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60eda75361b8600019f16c7c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"This is a picture of a Groyper-themed sticker.\" height=\"1234\" width=\"1650\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Groyper-Parody-Friend-Kekistan-Wrestlng/dp/B08VC3T2DW/ref=sr_1_1?dchild=1&#38;keywords=groyper&#38;qid=1626187220&#38;sr=8-1\" target=\"_blank\">Screenshot/Amazon</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>According to the meme-information website <a href=\"https://knowyourmeme.com/memes/groyper\">KnowYourMeme</a>, the Groyper meme format first sprouted on 4chan in 2015 and began to circulate more widely on online forums like 4chan and Reddit after 2017.</p><p>In 2019, Fuentes launched what would become known as the <a href=\"https://www.vox.com/policy-and-politics/2019/11/11/20948317/alt-right-donald-trump-jr-conservative-tpusa-yaf-racism-antisemitism\">&#34;Groyper Wars,&#34;</a> in which he encouraged his followers to attend events held by conservatives whom he deemed not far-right enough - including Donald Trump Jr., Turning Point USA founder Charlie Kirk, and right-wing commentator Ben Shapiro - and ask them provocative questions manufactured to &#34;expose&#34; the figures as &#34;fake&#34; conservatives. Fuentes, who also <a href=\"https://www.splcenter.org/hatewatch/2021/07/07/we-make-mistakes-twitters-embrace-extreme-far-right\">appeared at the 2017 &#34;Unite the Right&#34; rally</a> in Charlottesville, was <a href=\"https://www.motherjones.com/politics/2021/07/twitter-finally-bans-nick-fuentes/\">banned from Twitter last week</a> for violating the platform&#39;s rules. </p><p>Toward the end of 2020, <a href=\"https://www.splcenter.org/hatewatch/2021/01/19/meet-white-nationalist-organizer-who-spewed-hate-against-lawmakers\">Fuentes</a> encouraged his so-called Groypers to attend &#34;Stop the Steal&#34; events supporting the false idea that Donald Trump won the 2020 election and suggested followers join the US Capitol insurrection in January. Later that month, the FBI arrested one of those followers, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/ZTPetrizzo/status/1410748685231681537\">Anthime Gionet</a>, who went by the online pseudonym <a href=\"https://www.thedailybeast.com/how-donald-trump-jr-landed-smack-in-the-middle-of-a-right-wing-civil-war\">&#34;Baked Alaska&#34;</a> and has been linked to conspiracy theories and anti-semitism, for his role in storming the US Capitol.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.adl.org/resources/backgrounders/groyper-army\">The Anti-Defamation League</a> lists &#34;Groypers&#34; under its Extremism, Terrorism &#38; Bigotry section and defines the &#34;Groyper Army&#34; as a &#34;loose network of alt right figures,&#34; many of whom hold &#34;racist and anti-semitic views.&#34;</p><section 01:21:54","updatedTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:54","title":"Conservative MP Karl McCartney under investigation by Parliament's sleaze watchdog for hiding links to family firm","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/karl-mccartney-under-investigation-for-hiding-family-firm-links-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a7dd17f27b4c0019445e5f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"karl mccartney\" height=\"629\" width=\"1258\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Karl McCartney MP\n<p class=\"copyright\">Getty</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>EXCLUSIVE: Conservative MP Karl McCartney is under investigation by Parliament&#39;s sleaze watchdog.</li>\n<li>For more than a decade, McCartney has concealed his links to a family firm called Moonlighting Systems.</li>\n<li>The probe comes following an Insider investigation into McCartney&#39;s expenses and registered interests.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The Conservative MP Karl McCartney is under investigation by Parliament&#39;s sleaze watchdog after an Insider investigation revealed that he had made false declarations for more than a decade about his links to a family firm.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.theyworkforyou.com/regmem/?p=24790\">Since he was first elected in 2010</a>, McCartney has declared links to a firm he listed as ML Systems, an IT management and consultancy company, as an unpaid director and shareholder.</p><p>He declared payment for work done prior to his election in 2019, with the fee registered as being paid to the company.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/labour-demand-inquiry-into-conservative-mp-karl-mccartney-2021-6\">However, an investigation by Insider revealed</a> that McCartney was in fact tied to a different company, <a href=\"https://find-and-update.company-information.service.gov.uk/company/03666934/filing-history\">Moonlighting Systems</a>, whose sole director is McCartney&#39;s brother, Kevin.</p><p>Karl McCartney is listed as a secretary of the company and a minority shareholder.</p><p>Following Insider&#39;s reporting, Anneliese Dodds MP, the chair of the Labour Party, wrote to the Parliamentary Commissioner for Standards (PCS) asking for an investigation to be opened.</p><p>Now the PCS has <a href=\"https://www.parliament.uk/mps-lords-and-offices/standards-and-financial-interests/parliamentary-commissioner-for-standards/complaints-and-investigations/allegations-currently-under-investigation-by-the-commissioner/\">listed McCartney as being under investigation</a> regarding a issue of &#34;registration of interest.&#34;</p><p>Before the PCS announced her investigation, Dodds told Insider: &#34;If Karl McCartney is moonlighting, we need to know who for - and he shouldn&#39;t hide behind the name of a company that no longer exists.</p><p>&#34;The rules are there for a reason, the Conservatives can&#39;t just act as if they don&#39;t apply to them.&#34;</p><p>In <a href=\"https://www.bbc.co.uk/sounds/play/p09kzthw\">an interview with BBC Radio Lincolnshire</a>, McCartney said: &#34;It&#39;s all open and above board. I&#39;ve got nothing to hide.</p><p>&#34;That&#39;s the Labour Party for you. They&#39;ll throw as much mud as they can. My declaration on my register of members interests has been there for 11 years, obviously, since I was first elected. And it&#39;s exactly the same as it was back then as it is now.&#34;</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/conservative-mp-karl-mccartney-expenses-claim-donors-firm-2021-6\">Insider also revealed</a> McCartney had claimed more than £30,000 in public funds for Parliamentary work carried out by a company run by a donor who helped him become an MP in 2010. </p><p>McCartney concealed nearly £10,000 of those claims by declaring only that he was paying &#34;A&#34;, short for the real name of the company, Anagallis Communications. </p><p>But this will not be investigated by either the Parliamentary Commissioner for Standards or the Independent Parliamentary Standards Authority, as they say it does not breach rules on expenses claims.</p><p>Insider has contacted McCartney for comment, who has repeatedly declined to comment.</p><p>There is no suggestion of wrongdoing by McCartney&#39;s brother or Moonlighting Systems.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original new book says","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/facebook-new-book-mark-zuckerberg-people-or-sheryl-sandberg-people-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f370a4fe89ebf001f044f44?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Mark Zuckerberg sheryl sandberg\" height=\"1500\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Facebook&#39;s executives have Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Tension between Mark Zuckerberg and Sheryl Sandberg made employees &#34;Mark people&#34; or &#34;Sheryl people.&#34;</li>\n<li>The revelation comes from a new book, &#34;An Ugly Truth: Inside Facebook&#39;s Battle for Domination.&#34;</li>\n<li>One worker was reportedly &#34;puzzled about the public portrayal of them as amazing partners.&#34;</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>An early wedge between Facebook&#39;s leaders had ripple effects across the company, leading to most senior employees being unofficially designated either &#34;Mark people&#34; or &#34;Sheryl people,&#34; a new book says.</p><p>Facebook CEO Mark Zuckerberg &#34;wasn&#39;t all that interested in the details&#34; of the ad business COO Sheryl Sandberg was leading for Facebook and &#34;brushed off&#34; her requests for meetings, more staff, and a bigger budget, according to an advance copy of &#34;<a href=\"https://www.harpercollins.com/products/an-ugly-truth-sheera-frenkelcecilia-kang?variant=32999376551970\">An Ugly Truth: Inside Facebook&#39;s Battle for Domination</a>&#34; that Insider reviewed. </p><p>One employee on Facebook&#39;s business side told the book&#39;s authors, Sheera Frenkel and Cecilia Kang, that Zuckerberg was &#34;explicitly dismissive&#34; of Sandberg&#39;s remarks in some meetings. </p><p>&#34;I&#39;ve been consistently puzzled about the public portrayal of them as amazing partners,&#34; the employee said in the book.</p><p>Zuckerberg and Sandberg met at a Christmas party in 2007. Several conversations later, they agreed to have Sandberg join Facebook to focus on expanding advertising on the platform, which Zuckerberg had typically ignored in favor of expanding technological features, the book says.</p><p>&#34;She had thought, from his interest during their courtship dinners, that Zuckerberg was committed to strengthening the business and that he would be actively supportive of her role,&#34; the book says of Sandberg. &#34;As the weeks went by, though, it became apparent that she would have to fight to capture his attention.&#34; </p><p> The wedge between the company&#39;s leaders extended to their respective teams, separating tech and non-tech employees.</p><p>&#34;There was mutual distrust and annoyance,&#34; the book says. &#34;Engineers looked down on the &#39;marketing guys,&#39; and the business managers struggled to get into meetings with Zuckerberg&#39;s teams.&#34;</p><p>Tensions between the leaders led Sandberg to enlist Donald Graham, then a member of the company&#39;s board of directors, to &#34;lobby Zuckerberg for more resources on her behalf,&#34; according to the book.</p><p>&#34;His priority of growth was miles above advertising, revenue, and profits,&#34; Graham told the book&#39;s authors. &#34;It became my job to call him after every time Sheryl called and try to convince him about the importance of advertising, and not to change his priorities, but to help him move a little.&#34;</p><p>Facebook spokesperson Dani Lever denied any early tension between Zuckerberg and Sandberg. </p><p>&#34;This book tells a false narrative based on selective interviews, many from disgruntled individuals, and cherry-picked facts,&#34; Lever told Insider in a statement. &#34;The fault lines that the authors depict between Mark and Sheryl and the people who work with them do not exist. All of Mark&#39;s direct reports work closely with Sheryl and hers with Mark. Sheryl&#39;s role at the company has not changed.&#34; </p><p> </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a </li>\n<li>The CIO noted that technology stocks that dominate the S&#38;P 500 are at levels not seen since the peak of the dot-com bubble. </li>\n<li>The tech sector&#39;s profitability and earnings are vulnerable and could pose a risk to the broader market, she said.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\"></a><a href=\"https://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/10-things-opening-bell?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestdium=ingest?utm_source=markets&#38;utm_medium=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Sign up here for our daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell.</a></li>\n</ul><p>The odds of a stock market correction of up to 15% are rising as lofty technology stock valuations leave the broader market vulnerable, according to Morgan Stanley Wealth Management&#39;s chief investment officer.</p><p>In a Monday note, Lisa Shalett highlighted how low rates have helped prop up tech stocks to dot-com era valuations. The price to sales ratio of the technology sector is at a level not seen since the peak of the dot-com bubble in 2000, she said.</p><p>In addition, the tech sector now makes up a much larger weight in the <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/s&p_500_500\">S&#38;P 500</a> than in 2000, and has subsequently driven the price to sales ratio of the benchmark index to a level 50% higher than it has ever been. </p><p>&#34;The problem with this setup is that tech sector profitability and earnings are vulnerable,&#34; said Shalett. &#34;While secular growth trends may support resilience against small changes in economic growth, the sector now faces unprecedented headwinds from rising input costs, a weaker US dollar, fiercer competition, higher taxes, stricter regulations and customer backlash.&#34;</p><p>If those headwinds come to fruition for the technology sector, the broader market will be at risk. </p><p>She noted that markets tend to be strongest when they are broad based and there is a consensus narrative around what could go wrong in terms of economic outcomes, policy, geopolitics, and regulation. <br><br>&#34;As we have noted for the past two months, the market continues to grind to all-time highs on narrowing breadth, while the narrative has also grown increasingly muddled. Thus, the risks of a correction are rising,&#34; she said. </p><p>The chief investment officer of wealth management told clients to focus on stock-picking using earnings fundamentals. She also said investors could consider adding to financials stocks as a value-oriented hedge to rising rates. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60edbbafca74780018ae9189?format=jpeg\" the pandemic allowing workers to exchange high living costs for more <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/where-to-move-tech-engineers-jobs-austin-pittsburgh-raleigh-madison-2021-6\">affordable mid-size cities with larger houses.</a></p><p>Three of the cities with the highest concentrations of tech workers are in Canada, part of the US <a York City and San Francisco are still home to the most tech employees but smaller hubs like Nashville, Tennessee have seen the greatest gains.</p><p><em><strong>Read more: <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/where-to-move-tech-engineers-jobs-austin-pittsburgh-raleigh-madison-2021-6\">Tech workers and engineers are flocking to these 7 rising US cities - and not a single one is on the coasts</a></strong><strong><br></strong></em></p><p> Colin Yasukochi, the author of the CBRE report, said tech talent is the primary element driving a city&#39;s &#34;innovation infrastructure,&#34; which also includes education and research opportunities. </p><h2>The 10 unexpected cities where tech workers are flocking</h2><ol><li>Columbus, Ohio</li><li>Calgary, Towey)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f4e64117ed0ee001e25cb1e?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn11@2020_2/2021/07/13/17-22-26-123_811ef343b7bc0136.webp","https://i.insider.com/5f805fafea74820019ca6227?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn39@2020_6/2021/07/13/17-22-23-054_d65abe392552c558.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn12@2020_2/2021/07/13/17-22-25-174_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=8lYIhtHXS4Y:4YEJrtfbS5o:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn7@2020_3/2021/07/13/17-22-24-393_8632ba6a2fd99d81.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=8lYIhtHXS4Y:4YEJrtfbS5o:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn96@2020_5/2021/07/13/17-22-25-448_7686f4359651f1b4.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn83@2020_2/2021/07/13/17-22-23-761_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=8lYIhtHXS4Y:4YEJrtfbS5o:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn31@2020_3/2021/07/13/17-22-23-479_2f3168d2634cc1a6.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/8lYIhtHXS4Y":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn39@2020_6/2021/07/13/17-22-23-617_6716fafeabfe19b0.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626196914880},{"createdTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:54","updatedTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:54","title":"A health startup founder who raised $40 million plans to improve healthcare access in the US","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/founders-technology-democratize-medicine-startup-north-america-digital-medicine-doctors-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60eda65e61b8600019f16c73?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Rubicon founder\" height=\"1302\" width=\"1736\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Carlos Reines is the CEO and co-founder of RubiconMD.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Rubicon</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Health startup RubiconMD is revolutionizing the complex and costly healthcare model in the US.</li>\n<li>The platform allows primary care physicians to consult with specialists to improve patient care.</li>\n<li>Rubicon serves over 10 million Americans and has raised $40 million since it was founded in 2013.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Carlos Reines is the CEO and co-founder of RubiconMD.</p><p>As well as revolutionizing healthcare in the US, the founder raised more than $40 million since the start-up&#39;s inception in 2013. </p><p>Reines has been interested in healthcare since he was a child, but instead of going into medicine, he opted for telecommunications engineering - Reines says this was because he thought tech would be a better way to make a difference in improving people&#39;s access to healthcare. </p><p>He studied at the Polytechnic University of Madrid, Spain, and obtained a specialization in Biomedical Engineering at the Technical University of Delft in the Netherlands. </p><p>He started his career in digital health at Siemens Medical in Pennsylvania and prior to RubiconMD, he managed a division at Telefónica. </p><p>Reines told Insider he was named a Young Global Leader by the World Economic Forum and has an MBA from Harvard, which was the starting point for Rubicon.</p><p>Reines got involved in all the events with startups during the master&#39;s degree and at one such event, he met the man who would become his partner in founding RubiconMD.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60eda82e61b8600019f16c83?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Telemedicine online doctor appointment\" height=\"2800\" width=\"3734\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>&#34;What we do in the US works very well because we connect primary care with the specialist so that they do a remote consultation.&#34;\n<p class=\"copyright\">BSIP/Universal Images Group via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Gil Addo is also passionate about trying to improve access to healthcare in the United States. </p><p>&#34;We hit on the idea of collaborating together and so we got started in one weekend,&#34; said Reines. They both won a competition for best pitch, which encouraged them to pursue the idea and they ended up registering the company. </p><p>While all his fellow master&#39;s students were looking for a place in a big company that summer, Reines decided to bet everything on RubiconMD and turn it into his own project. </p><p>&#34;I went to New York and we set up the company that summer and made a small pilot,&#34; he explained. </p><p>Rubicon MD is a platform that connects primary care doctors with specialists so that they can consult with patients to avoid unnecessary referrals and make more accurate diagnoses. </p><p>The pilot, in which Reines had to work almost manually on a consultation-by-consultation basis, yielded information from more than 200 consultations. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60eda850ca74780018ae90f9?format=jpeg\" alt=\"healthcare\" height=\"1332\" width=\"1776\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Reines says the US healthcare system is very unequal: &#34;Half the country may not have access to a specialist.&#34;\n<p class=\"copyright\">Photo by Win McNamee/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>&#34;It allowed us to understand the system from the inside, what things needed to be optimized,&#34; explains Reines. </p><p>The feedback was decisive: the primary care doctor who took part in the pilot confirmed that in the last two months using the platform he had had more interaction with other doctors than in the last 10 years. </p><p>Rubicon improved the quality of care that primary care physicians can provide to patients who might not otherwise be able to access a specialist or would end up making an emergency room visit. </p><p>From there, the founders sought funding and Reines combined the second year of his master&#39;s degree - turning down an offer to help him with the project on the condition that he leave the master&#39;s.</p><p>What little savings the engineer did have had gone into his MBA. He even slept on his partner&#39;s sofa. </p><p>&#34;It was a tough time, but at the same time super nice because we took a leap of faith and it was all working out,&#34; he said. </p><p>In the first year, the startup raised $1.5 million, mostly through angel investors and some funds and medical groups.</p><h2><strong>Why the US system needed Rubicon </strong></h2><p>&#34;The healthcare system in the US is a very complex system,&#34; Reines said. &#34;It&#39;s the most expensive system in the world and they don&#39;t do any better than countries that spend half as much.&#34;  </p><p>&#34;The main problem is that it is a very unequal system,&#34; he says. &#34;Half the country may not have access to a specialist.&#34;</p><p>&#34;What we do in the US works very well because we connect primary care with the specialist so that they do a remote consultation. The specialist reviews your question and shares some impressions and recommendations about how they normally treat these types of cases and with that input the family doctor makes a more informed decision about diagnosis and treatment for their patients,&#34; he said.</p><p>Reines says that 80% of the time, this results in a very significant improvement in the patient&#39;s care plan and almost half of the time avoids what would have been an unnecessary referral to a specialist, &#34;thereby offloading the system and reducing unnecessary costs.&#34; </p><h2>The platform has already served 10 million patients</h2><p>Rubicon is now present in nearly 40 states across the country and has hired employees in each of them. </p><p>Thousands of doctors already use the platform and the number of patients under the care of these doctors has &#34;already exceeded 10 million,&#34; the entrepreneur said. </p><p>Who are RubiconMD&#39;s customers?  &#34;Well, mainly the most innovative medical groups,&#34; says Reines. </p><p>The country is experiencing a boom in companies that are transforming primary care, and Reines says that &#34;most of them are already customers&#34;. </p><p>&#34;We have found a niche in clinics that have an incentive to improve quality and reduce total cost, rather than a pay-for-service,&#34; he said. </p><p>RubiconMD also works with companies that have an in-office clinic, including &#34;some of the largest technology companies on the West Coast,&#34;as well as assembly-line factories and factories in rural areas. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60eda8aaca74780018ae90fd?format=jpeg\" alt=\"wind farm in Iowa\" height=\"3555\" width=\"4740\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Rubicon is extending better healthcare to more remote areas, too.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jonathan Ernst/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>On the other hand, RubiconMD is also used by a number of clinics known in the US as safety-net clinics, where people with the most basic insurance (which doesn&#39;t cover specialist costs or even papers) can be seen. </p><p>For Reines, this is the best illustration of the startup&#39;s philosophy and mission.</p><p>&#34;Maybe the patient in a practice is an executive in a technology company, who might have access to the specialist in another way. But, at the same time, you are also seeing the patient who has no insurance, or no papers, who works part-time and can&#39;t make time to go to the doctor. They would never be able to go to see the kind of top-notch specialist that we are bringing in&#34;. </p><p>&#34;Our mission as a company is to democratize access to healthcare,&#34; he said. </p><p>For now, however, Rubicon MD has its hands full with the USUnited States, although one of its short-term priorities is to continue hiring Spanish talent to expand the subsidiary in Spain. </p><p>&#34;In terms of service, what we have done is to go deeper into certain specialties and some types of conditions. For example, mental health,&#34; said Reines.</p><p>&#34;Primary care can help a lot to solve patients&#39; mental health problems, which are also closely linked to their physical health,&#34; he added. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60eda921ca74780018ae9114?format=jpeg\" alt=\"migrant children us-mexico border\" height=\"1342\" width=\"1789\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Rubicon works with a number of NGOs that send doctors to treat families on the ground, to avoid separating them at all costs.\n<p class=\"copyright\">John Moore/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>&#34;We created a service that basically allows primary care doctors to manage patients with mental health issues much better, with remote support from a psychiatrist,&#34; said Reines. &#34;The platform has a database of each patient, which allows them to follow their progress and a question and answer session can be organized.&#34; </p><p>Reines said that they plan to do the same with chronic diseases.</p><p>As for going international, though RubiconMD is focused on the US market, the startup carries out impact and non-profit projects in areas where there&#39;s a greater need.<strong> </strong></p><p>&#34;For example, on the US-Mexico border there are refugee camps for people who have fled violence in their country and are waiting to cross into the United States,&#34; Reines said. When a child gets sick, they can be treated in the US, but it&#39;s naturally a difficult decision for the parents as they don&#39;t know when they&#39;ll see them again. </p><p>Rubicon works with a number of NGOs that send doctors to treat families on the ground, to avoid separating them at all costs.<strong> </strong></p><p>They do similar work at a children&#39;s malnutrition clinic in Haiti, another for underprivileged patients in the Dominican Republic, and a series of clinics in Nigeria.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 01:21:54","updatedTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:54","title":"14 pitch decks that startups looking to disrupt media and advertising used to raise millions","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/pitch-decks-that-advertising-media-startups-used-to-raise-millions-2021-6","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60be65f893c6fa00195e58b3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Restream founders\" height=\"1280\" width=\"1706\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Restream cofounders Andrew Surzynskyi and Alex Khuda.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Restream</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Investors are pouring money into advertising, media, and marketing startups.</li>\n<li>They&#39;re trying to capitalize on changing consumer habits and marketers&#39; need to ensure their ads are working.</li>\n<li>Check out these pitch decks to see how these startups pitched their visions to VCs and other investors.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Investors are pouring money into startups that are trying to disrupt advertising, media, and marketing.</p><p>Insider has been tracking these startups that are using tech to capitalize on changing consumer media habits and marketers&#39; desire to reach new audiences and ensure their ads are working.</p><p>Check out these pitch decks that they&#39;ve used to sell their vision and raise millions from PE and VC investors.</p><p>They range from tools that measure digital ad performance to platforms for people seeking out online entertainment.</p><hr><h2>Data management tools</h2><p>Google and Apple&#39;s moves to clamp down on third-party cookies and the rise of online shopping have advertisers clamoring for help managing all their customer data so they can effectively market to them.</p><p>One such company is 4-year-old Amperity, which sells software that clients like Starbucks, Patagonia, and Crocs use to manage stats from sales, email, e-commerce, and loyalty card programs.</p><p><strong>Amperity has raised $100 million in its Series D</strong> from existing investors including Tiger Global Management, Declaration Partners, and Madrona Venture Group, for a total of $187 million.</p><h2><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amperitys-series-d-100-million-fundraise-investor-pitch-deck-2021-7\">Here&#39;s the pitch deck that helped a marketing tech startup raise $100 million at a $1 billion valuation to help brands manage their data</a></h2><hr><h2>Out-of-home advertising platform</h2><p>Outdoor advertising is coming back after being crushed during the pandemic, and adtech startup OneScreen.ai is hoping to cash in with a platform for brands to search, buy, run and measure their out-of-home ad campaigns.</p><p><strong>OneScreen just raised $1.2 million</strong> in pre-seed funding in a round led by Florida-based fund TechFarms Capital with other investors including HubSpot cofounders Brian Halligan and Dharmesh Shah, Wayfair&#39;s alumni fund Wayfund, Lola.com CEO Mike Volpe, and BuySellAds.com CEO Todd Garland.</p><h2><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/onescreenai-has-raised-1-million-to-transform-outdoor-advertising-2021-7\">See the pitch deck that Google, Hubspot and Wayfair alums used to raise $1.2 million to build the &#39;Amazon of out-of-home advertising&#39;</a></h2><hr><h2>Consumer data-collection</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60d9b282df1db80018f3a7c3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Jeffrey Nicholson\" height=\"3777\" width=\"5037\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Jeffrey Nicholson.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Tracer</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Tracer started in 2015 as a unit of Gary Vaynerchuk&#39;s ad agency VaynerMedia that automatically collects and organize data that isn&#39;t personally identifiable. Led by Tracer co-founder and CEO Jeffrey Nicholson, it also offers free consulting services. It started by helping VaynerMedia oversee hundreds of millions in ad buys for clients like Oreo maker Mondelez; today, clients include other ad agencies like Labelium; Condé Nast; and pharma giant Sanofi.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tracer-raises-99-million-seed-round-marc-lore-kevin-durant-2021-6\"><strong>Tracer recently raised $9.9 million in seed funding</strong></a> led by big names like former Walmart and Amazon exec Marc Lore and NBA star Kevin Durant&#39;s firm Thirty Five Ventures.</p><h2><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pitch-deck-for-data-startup-tracer-that-raised-nearly-10-million-2021-6\">Read the pitch deck a Gary Vaynerchuk-backed data startup used to raise $10 million from investors like Walmart&#39;s ex-ecommerce CEO</a></h2><hr><h2>Building lifetime customers</h2><p>As people do more of their shopping online, marketers are trying to get them to become repeat customers.</p><p>Former Paypal and Facebook product and data analytics manager Emad Hasan says his startup Retina helps brands like Dollar Shave Club and Madison Reed acquire and keep customers by building lookalike audiences based on companies&#39; order history and shopper attributes.</p><p><strong>It just raised $8 million in Series A funding</strong> from Alpha Intelligence Capital, Vertical Venture Partners, and others. </p><h2><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pitch-deck-customer-insights-startup-retina-raises-8-million-2021-6\">This investor deck helped a former Facebook product manager raise $8 million to help brands boost customers&#39; long-term value</a></h2><hr><h2>Data-buying tools</h2><p>Nick Jordan founded 5-year-old Narrative to let advertisers buy data without the need for data brokers like Epsilon and Acxiom that can be known for not disclosing their data sources or what cut they take.</p><p>The marketing-tech firm makes money by taking a cut of data sales and through larger software as a Service (or SaaS) contracts where marketers pay monthly fees for data.</p><p><strong>Narrative in September raised $8.5 million in a Series A funding round</strong> led by G20 Ventures and which included Glasswing Ventures and MathCapital, bringing its total funding to $14 million.</p><h2><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/marketing-tech-firm-narratives-series-a-pitch-deck-2020-2020-10?r=ad-media-pitch-decks-lp\">Here&#39;s the investor deck that helped startup Narrative raise $8.5 million to help marketers buy data safely</a></h2><hr><h2>Support for online sellers</h2><p>Adtech vet Paul Palmieri joined Tradeswell as CEO based on his experience as a VC investor, where he saw dozens of DTC companies whose businesses weren&#39;t scalable.</p><p>Tradeswell is a SaaS platform that consolidates brands&#39; marketing, retail, inventory, logistics, forecasting, lifetime value and financial information. Its pitch is that it gives brands insights so they know what to sell to whom, where, and at what price.</p><p>US e-commerce is set to be worth $1 trillion by 2023, according to a recent report by Insider Intelligence&#39;s eMarketer, and Tradeswell says it can help traditional and DTC brands save millions of dollars in outsourced contracts and boost their sales.</p><p><strong>Tradeswell recently raised $3.3 million in seed round funding from Signalfire and Construct Capital.</strong></p><h2><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/adtech-vet-paul-palmieri-investor-deck-e-commerce-platform-2020-10?r=ad-media-pitch-decks-lp\">This investor deck helped an entrepreneur raise $3.3 million to build &#39;the Bloomberg terminal&#39; for online sellers </a></h2><hr><h2>Ad performance tools</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60be6751e459cb0018a2c84b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"BrandTotal\" height=\"1400\" width=\"1866\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">BrandTotal</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>BrandTotal is a marketing analytics company that pitches advertisers on the premise that most digital and social media ads are now &#34;dark,&#34; or visible only to the people they&#39;re targeting. </p><p>It joins other businesses that promise greater visibility into digital advertising such as Pathmatics, which measures how much brands spend on Facebook and other platforms.</p><p>BrandTotal co-founder Alon Leibovich said the company uses AI to track ads and help advertisers understand their competitors&#39; strategies. </p><p><strong>This pitch has helped BrandTotal win business from big brands like L&#39;Oréal and raise $12 million in a Series B funding round, bringing its total funding to $20 million. </strong></p><p>Canada&#39;s INcapital Ventures led the latest round along with Maor Investments, Glilot Capital Partners, Flint Capital, KDC Media Fund, and FJ Labs.</p><h2><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tech-platform-brandtotal-raised-20-million-with-this-investor-deck-2020-9?r=ad-media-pitch-decks-lp\">This investor deck helped startup BrandTotal raise $20 million to date to help advertisers like L&#39;Oréal see how their digital ads are working</a></h2><hr><h2>E-commerce advertising services</h2><p>Brands are increasingly becoming advertising platforms, giving rise to a cottage industry of adtech companies that help marketers build their own ad businesses.</p><p>One such firm is 9-year-old adtech firm Adzerk, which is rebranding as Kevel. </p><p>EMarketer reports that e-commerce advertising will be a $17 billion market this year. Retailers like Walgreens, Walmart, and Instacart have led the charge, but Kevel sees an opportunity for other types of brands to build ad businesses of their own.</p><p><strong>In December, Kevel raised $11 million in a Series A round led by Fulcrum Equity with Commerce Ventures, MathCapital and Food Retail Ventures also participating.</strong></p><h2><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/kevel-raises-11-million-help-build-in-house-ad-businesses-2020-12?r=ad-media-pitch-decks-lp\">A digital ad firm just raised $11 million to help brands like United Airlines and Ticketmaster build their own ad businesses</a></h2><hr><h2>Targeted ad tools</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60be678493c6fa00195e58b8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Mathieu Roche, CEO of ID5\" height=\"1014\" width=\"1353\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">ID5</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Google&#39;s and Apple&#39;s moves to clamp down on privacy and digital-ad targeting have been a boon for startups trying to find workarounds like identity solutions.</p><p>One such firm is ID5, a European startup that helps advertisers find audiences to target and make sure people don&#39;t repeatedly see the same ads. It makes money from licensing its ID to adtech companies for a monthly fee that ranges from $5,000 to $30,000, CEO Mathieu Roche said. The company gives away its technology to publishers to grow adoption of the ID.</p><p><strong>ID5 closed a $6 million Series A funding round in March from Alliance Entreprendre, Progress Ventures, and 360 Capital Partners.</strong> The 4-year-old company has raised a total of $7.5 million.</p><h2><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/id5-series-a-pitch-deck-to-save-digital-ad-targeting-2021-3?r=ad-media-pitch-decks-lp\">Read the pitch deck that a startup used to raise $6 million to save targeted advertising</a></h2><hr><h2>Privacy compliance help</h2><p>New privacy regulations are springing up around the globe, and publishers and marketers are turning to technology companies to stay on the right side of these laws and avoid huge fines.</p><p>One of the companies capitalizing on the increased focus on data privacy is Sourcepoint. Founded by adtech vets Ben Barokas and Brian Kane, the US-based technology company has a platform that lets publishers and advertisers get legal consent from people to use their data.</p><p><strong>Sourcepoint recently raised $17 million in additional funding, led by new investor Arrowroot Capital,</strong> bringing its total funding to $47.8 million since it launched in 2015.</p><h2><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pitch-deck-privacy-compliance-platform-sourcepoint-raises-17-million-2020-12?r=ad-media-pitch-decks-lp\">The pitch deck used to raise $17 million for a startup that helps advertisers and publishers comply with privacy laws</a></h2><hr><h2>Real-time market research</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f68f96f323fc4001e0d78c7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Former CEO of Publicis agency MRY and Suzy CEO Matt Britton\" height=\"883\" width=\"1178\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Matt Britton</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Agency veteran Matt Britton pitches his consumer intelligence startup Suzy as an always-on digital assistant like Siri or Alexa for marketers. It has a panel of 1 million US consumers that lets marketers conduct surveys and research on subjects like product development and ad effectiveness testing.</p><p><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/ex-agency-exec-matt-britton-wants-to-challenge-nielsen-qualtrics-2020-9\">He closed a $34 million Series C round last year</a>, bringing its total raised to $46 million</strong>.</p><p>Rho Ventures, Bertelsmann Digital Media Investments, Triangle Peak Partners, and Foundry Group participated in the Series C round in March ($18 million) and September ($16 million).</p><h2><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pitch-deck-agency-vet-matt-britton-market-research-platform-suzy-2020-9#suzy-sells-itself-as-a-human-intelligence-platform-that-helps-companies-make-better-and-more-informed-decisions-faster-1?r=ad-media-pitch-decks-lp\">An agency vet used this pitch deck to sell what he called the &#39;Siri for marketers,&#39; landing clients including Johnson &#38; Johnson and Chipotle</a></h2><hr><h2><strong>Livestreaming tools for creators</strong></h2><p>Livestreaming startup Restream was founded in 2015 to help gaming content creators grow their reach by livestreaming to Twitch and YouTube at the same time.</p><p>It&#39;s since expanded to serve musicians, politicians, influencers, publishers, non-profit organizations, and other businesses and says its goal is to democratize broadcasting. Restream said half its 2.5 million users are now non-gamers. Most of its users are nonpaying, but it sells subscriptions from $19 to $299 per month that come with features like the ability to record streams and access to more customer support.</p><p><strong>Restream announced in August that it had raised $50 million in fresh funding from investors including Sapphire Ventures and Insight Partners.</strong></p><h2><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/livestreaming-startup-restream-pitch-deck-50-million-raise-2020-9?r=ad-media-pitch-decks-lp\">Read the 14-slide pitch deck that helped livestreaming startup Restream raise $50 million amid the pandemic </a></h2><hr><h2><strong>Video streaming subscriptions</strong><strong><br></strong></h2><p>CuriosityStream is a 5-year-old streaming service founded by former Discovery Communications founder John Hendricks. It went public in fall 2020 through a reverse merger with Software Acquisition Group, a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-a-spac\">SPAC</a> led by Jonathan Huberman, who formerly led video adtech firm Ooyala.</p><p>CuriosityStream is differentiated from other streaming services in that it focuses on factual content like documentaries and features, with more than 3,100 titles available. It reported 13 million paying subscribers buying monthly and yearly subscriptions ranging from $3 a month to $70 a year.</p><p><strong>The deal with Software Acquisition Group gave CuriosityStream $180 million in cash.</strong></p><h2><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/curiousitystreams-2020-spac-road-show-investor-deck-2020-10?r=ad-media-pitch-decks-lp\">The investor deck that CuriosityStream used to secure $180 million to take on rival video streaming services</a></h2><hr><h2><strong>Reaching online sports fans</strong></h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60be67ac93c6fa00195e58b9?format=jpeg\" alt=\"overtime founder\" height=\"946\" width=\"1262\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Overtime</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Overtime wants to be the next ESPN, but for social media.</p><p>It started<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/overtime-app-raises-25-million-seed-round-2017-2\"> 2016</a> by Endeavor vets Dan Porter and Zack Weiner with a focus on high-school sports and athletes and has expanded into areas <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/inside-sports-startup-overtimes-expansion-into-esports-gaming-2019-12\">including esports</a>. </p><p>Overtime captures game highlights through people it pays to film events and also creates original programming and events. It distributes content mainly on social platforms like YouTube, Instagram, and TikTok. </p><p>Its core business is making money from ads, sponsorships, and merchandise, and projects making $200 million in annual revenue by 2024.</p><p><strong>It recently raised $80 million from investors including Amazon founder Jeff Bezos, rapper Drake, and Reddit cofounder Alexis Ohanian, <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/overtime-raises-80-million-from-jeff-bezos-drake-nba-stars-and-others-11619087409\">The Wall Street Journal recently reported</a>.</strong></p><h2><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/overtime-deck-how-it-reaches-sports-fans-raised-80-million-2021-4?r=ad-media-pitch-decks-lp\">Leaked pitch deck shows how sports-media startup Overtime plans to reach $200 million in revenue by 2024</a></h2><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a (Anna Popp,Tercius Bufete)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5d5da4e3bbb7c6072f04ce47?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn35@2020_1/2021/07/13/17-22-05-092_9a49936d6f51044a.webp","https://i.insider.com/60ecaa2061b8600019f16b28?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn27@2020_5/2021/07/13/17-22-25-073_3f6f2eb9660d1eec.webp","https://i.insider.com/5d28b72ca17d6c3704184769?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn71@2020_1/2021/07/13/17-22-22-005_613c385275d989c0.webp","https://i.insider.com/5c41e6b010f0d053ff2cb7b9?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn10@2020_1/2021/07/13/17-22-22-594_71d7d0bd5b24c84a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn12@2020_2/2021/07/13/17-22-25-174_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=_ge-mdoptUs:s_F9MlSI3Hc:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn71@2020_3/2021/07/13/17-22-24-155_41c8814a00b27bd2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=_ge-mdoptUs:s_F9MlSI3Hc:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn75@2020_1/2021/07/13/17-22-25-017_a3956a29f998442c.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn83@2020_2/2021/07/13/17-22-23-761_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=_ge-mdoptUs:s_F9MlSI3Hc:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn4@2020_4/2021/07/13/17-22-24-076_36c4d3d38a6db115.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/_ge-mdoptUs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn19@2020_2/2021/07/13/17-22-26-011_a6b0bdc5209c94fa.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626196914896},{"createdTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:54","updatedTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:54","title":"I'm a millionaire businessman who was arrested for protesting with restaurant workers. We demand better wages for the employees running our economy.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/business-economy-worker-shortage-restaurants-rights-wages-protest-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60e74ec9c03e9c0018ab2916?format=jpeg\" alt=\"wage protest\" height=\"1500\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Andrew Burton/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>What our economy is experiencing is not a worker shortage, it&#39;s a wage shortage. </li>\n<li>Our economic recovery is stalling because wages have been frozen for a decade.</li>\n<li>It&#39;s time we give America&#39;s tipped workers the pay increase they deserve. Our countries financial future relies on it.</li>\n<li>Brian is a member of the <a href=\"https://patrioticmillionaires.org/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://patrioticmillionaires.org/&source=gmail&ust=1625796014598000&usg=AFQjCNHF6G-hMQsbqzbBZrdzpMxKGvo6YAdzpMxKGvo6YA\">Patriotic Millionaires</a> and the co-founder of The Delta Fund.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>As the US transitions into the recovery phase of the pandemic, tipped workers across the country are leveraging their strength in numbers and<a href=\"https://money.yahoo.com/expert-great-wage-revolt-among-restaurant-workers-193807846.html\"> sending a clear message</a> to the restaurant industry that they should be paid what they deserve.</p><p>The sub-minimum wage for tipped workers is a direct legacy of slavery that has long contributed to some of <a href=\"https://www.eater.com/2017/12/7/16746064/sexual-harassment-restaurant-workers-data-servers-cooks-bartenders\">the highest rates</a> of sexual harassment across any industry. It&#39;s time policymakers take action to ensure one fair wage nationwide. </p><p>On May 25, I joined restaurant workers in downtown San Francisco as part of a nationwide wage strike to demand an end to the sub-minimum wage and a full, fair living wage nationwide. We engaged in civil disobedience to call attention to the ongoing injustice that tipped minimum wage workers are forced to endure every day, and were arrested by SFPD as a result. </p><p>As a wealthy white man, my experience being arrested was likely more comfortable than the conditions many of our nation&#39;s tipped workers face every day. <a href=\"https://www.cbsnews.com/news/sexual-harassment-restaurant-industry-70-percent/\">70%</a> of women working as servers, bartenders, or other roles in the food services industry say they&#39;ve dealt with sexual harassment from their employers, coworkers or customers. COVID-19 has only exacerbated these issues and made working conditions worse for vulnerable employees. </p><p>Now, with our country facing an unprecedented hiring shortage, especially in the restaurant industry, it is slowing our economic recovery. Hard working Americans simply don&#39;t want to risk their lives for poverty wages any longer. It&#39;s important that allies in California, which is already a One Fair Wage state - a state that requires all employers to pay the full minimum wage with fair, non-discriminatory tips on top - with a stronger restaurant industry to prove it, join this fight.</p><p>I am a successful business leader, a former executive, and now an investor in old and new businesses across the United States, so I know what a good investment looks like.  I&#39;ve done the research and seen for myself how ending the sub-minimum wage and enacting a full, fair minimum wage with tips on top is not only good for restaurant workers, but for owners and customers as well.  Pre-pandemic, the seven existing One Fair Wage states have<a href=\"https://onefairwage.site/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/OFW_FederalFactSheet_3-1.pdf\"> higher</a> restaurant industry growth and even higher rates of tipping. Even now, though all restaurants have struggled mightily in the face of COVID-19 shutdowns, restaurants in One Fair Wage states have on average seen<a href=\"https://onefairwage.site/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/OFW_DeclineHospBus_3.pdf\"> less decline</a> in their number of open businesses in the hospitality industry. </p><p>But don&#39;t take it from me. Take it from the heads of the corporate restaurant chains that have long been fighting against raising wages.<a href=\"https://www.newsweek.com/mcdonalds-other-ceos-tell-investors-15-minimum-wage-wont-hurt-business-1580978\"> On call after call</a>, these CEOs have not only said that a higher minimum wage for all workers doesn&#39;t hurt their business, they&#39;ve also admitted that it&#39;s actually <em>better</em> for business. </p><p>The CFO of Denny&#39;s, for instance, said on an investor call that California raising its minimum wage has helped the chain outperform there versus the rest of the country. Understandably, that&#39;s led to a<a href=\"https://www.newsweek.com/dennys-shareholders-revolt-after-ceo-concedes-15-minimum-wage-wont-hurt-business-1588970\"> shareholder revolt</a> against the company&#39;s continued lobbying against a $15 minimum wage. If companies like Denny&#39;s admit that One Fair Wage is good for their bottom line, they&#39;re violating their fiduciary duty by spending millions of dollars lobbying against fair wage laws.</p><p>That&#39;s why our protest in San Francisco started outside Denny&#39;s downtown. We need to hold them accountable for their hypocrisy and the low-wages they&#39;re still paying our brothers and sisters across the country. </p><p>The bottom line is that the federal government has already bailed out restaurant owners to the tune of over $28 billion over the last year and a half. It&#39;s time for the federal government to give restaurant workers the same attention, and mandate that they must be paid what they deserve.</p><p>The House has acted. Now, we need the Senate to pass the full Raise the Wage Act, which would end subminimum wages for tipped workers and make a $15 minimum wage the law of the land.  </p><p>As a business executive and investor, I know that what&#39;s good for people is good for business. We&#39;re a consumer-driven economy, and putting more money in the hands of workers is essential to driving demand. On the flip side, smart business leaders know that inequality is bad for the economy and bad for business. With the pandemic driving more profits and government bailouts into the hands of the ownership class while impoverishing and bankrupting workers, we&#39;re all going to end up worse off unless a drastic change is made. </p><p>Restaurants don&#39;t have a worker shortage, they have a wage shortage. That&#39;s why I stood in solidarity with restaurant workers and was arrested alongside them in their nationwide wage strike. It&#39;s time we demand better for everyone. Call your representatives and let our leaders know that we demand a just and thriving economy, and therefore we demand giving all workers a living wage.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Sign up here for our daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell.</a></li>\n</ul><p>TikTok has banned creators from publishing sponsored content related to finance including investment services and cryptocurrencies. <br><br><a href=\"https://www.ftadviser.com/your-industry/2021/07/08/tiktok-bans-investment-promotions/\">The Financial Times</a> first reported last week that the social media platform updated its <a href=\"https://support.tiktok.com/en/business-and-creator/creator-and-business-accounts/branded-content-policy\">branded content policy,</a> which bans the promotion of industries like alcohol, weapons, and gambling, to include financial services on its list of prohibited content.</p><p>Tik Tok said its policy included but was not limited to cryptocurrency, trading platforms, investment services, get rick quick schemes, foreign exchange, debit and pre-payment cards, forex trading, and others. </p><p>T<a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/tiktok-investing-advice-rate-review-financial-experts-stock-market-education-2021-6\">he social media platform is awash with financial content</a>, with the hashtag &#34;#investing&#34; gaining over 2.8 billion views. The ban appears to only apply to sponsored content, not general videos discussing cryptocurrencies and investments. <br><br><a href=\"https://www.tiktok.com/@errol_coleman?lang=en\">Errol Coleman</a>, a TikTok financial content creator with 264,000 followers, said the recent news that a <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/faze-clan-save-the-kids-cryptocurrency-scam-controversy-2021-7\">large esports organization was promoting a token that could have been a scam</a> on social media may have propelled TikTok to tighten its policies.</p><p>&#34;There are many accounts now promoting questionable cryptos and other investments,&#34; he added. &#34;I believe that is where TikTok is seeing the issue.&#34;<br><br>Coleman doesn&#39;t post sponsored investment content and therefore won&#39;t be affected by the ban. </p><p>TikTok&#39;s ban comes as financial regulators warn investors to watch out for fraudulent investing advice and information. In December, <a href=\"https://www.sec.gov/oiea/investor-alerts-and-bulletins/investment-scam-complaints-rise-investor-alert\">the SEC said</a> it experienced a significant uptick in tips, complaints, and referrals involving investment scams. <br><br>The social media platform said its branded content policy is &#34;designed to ensure a safe and positive environment&#34; for TikTok users. src=\"https://i.insider.com/60edbf4eca74780018ae919e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Elon Musk at Delaware Chancery Court sketch\" height=\"2268\" width=\"4032\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Tesla CEO Elon Musk in 2016.</li>\n<li>Things got testy between Musk and the plaintiffs&#39; attorney. </li>\n<li>Musk said he hates running Tesla and could have worked on Wall Street. </li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Elon Musk <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-court-tesla-solarcity-acquisition-energy-damages-2021-7\">took the stand</a> on Monday to defend Tesla&#39;s 2016 acquisition of a struggling solar firm founded by his cousins. It went about as smoothly as you&#39;d expect a five-hour testimony from an outspoken billionaire with practically no filter would go. </p><p>That is to say, things got off-topic and, at some points, pretty testy. </p><p>A group of Tesla shareholders is suing Musk over the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-tesla-solarcity-merger-frenzied-plan-new-filings-show-2019-10\">purchase of SolarCity</a>, alleging that his role as its chairman and largest shareholder presented a conflict of interest. They claim that Musk pressured Tesla&#39;s board into greenlighting the $2.6 billion purchase and want Musk to pay back $2 billion to the electric-vehicle maker.</p><p>Other members of the board have already settled to the tune of $60 million.</p><p>Musk maintains that he did not exert any influence over the board as it made the decision and pushed back against claims that it was a bailout, multiple <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/business/musk-testify-defense-teslas-26-bln-deal-solarcity-2021-07-12/\">outlets</a> <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/technology/2021/07/12/elon-musk-trial-tesla/\">reported</a>. He also reiterated that the deal was a stock-for-stock transaction that didn&#39;t benefit him financially and that it was always part of Tesla&#39;s plan to move beyond electric-vehicle production into clean-energy solutions. </p><p>Still, much of the day saw Musk sparring with the shareholders&#39; main attorney, Randy Baron, and giving meandering answers that got off-topic. Here are five of the most notable moments:</p><h2>Musk &#34;hates&#34; running Tesla</h2><p>Musk at one point said he doesn&#39;t want to be Tesla&#39;s CEO but fears that the company would falter without him. </p><p>&#34;I tried very hard not to be the CEO of Tesla, but I have to or frankly Tesla is going to die,&#34; Musk said, according to <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2021-07-12/elon-musk-tells-court-tesla-s-solarcity-deal-wasn-t-a-bailout?sref=LspfQlRv\">Bloomberg</a>. &#34;I rather hate being a boss. I&#39;m an engineer.&#34; </p><p>Musk, who also serves as CEO of SpaceX, a rocket firm he founded, has <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-says-he-is-impulsive-does-not-like-ceo-template-tesla-2018-12\">said</a> similar things before. Tesla itself acknowledges in regulatory filings that it relies heavily on Musk and that it would be in a tough spot if he left the company. </p><h2>&#34;I think you are a bad human being.&#34;</h2><p>Sparks flew between Musk and Baron, the plaintiffs&#39; lawyer, in pre-trial depositions. Monday was no exception.</p><p>Asked why he was being &#34;derisive&#34; in his deposition, Musk retorted by pointing out a history of criminal activity at a law firm Baron used to work at. </p><p>&#34;You were mentored by criminals,&#34; Musk said, according to <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2021-07-12/elon-musk-tells-court-tesla-s-solarcity-deal-wasn-t-a-bailout?sref=LspfQlRv\">Bloomberg</a>. &#34;Then you continued to be mentored by criminals and that is why I do not respect you. I think you are a bad human being.&#34;</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> </em><em><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-solar-panels-roof-energy-leaks-arbitration-elon-musk-2021-6\">A couple says their Tesla Solar panels caused relentless leaks that led to mold 10 times the healthy limit, $115,000 in damages, and a long-running legal battle</a></em></p><h2>&#34;I think I&#39;m funny.&#34;</h2><p>Baron asked if Tesla&#39;s board approved Musk&#39;s title change to Technoking in March, and Musk responded that it was a joke that was <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-tesla-technoking-jokes-funny-free-press-court-solarcity-2021-7\">aimed at getting the carmaker free press</a>. The company <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-proved-tesla-doesnt-need-advertising-2020-5\">has no advertising budget</a>, and Musk is known for leaning into <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-tesla-model-s-price-cut-lucid-unveils-air-2020-10\">memes</a> and internet culture.  </p><p>&#34;It generated a whole bunch of free press and Tesla doesn&#39;t advertise and it&#39;s helpful to general sales,&#34; he said, per <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/business/musk-testify-defense-teslas-26-bln-deal-solarcity-2021-07-12/\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"e8cab0a492e155d8bfaf50bb9ecb666c\">Reuters</a>. </p><p>&#34;I think I&#39;m funny,&#34; Musk added. </p><h2>Musk denied &#34;rage-firing&#34; anyone.</h2><p>Pushing back against claims that he ousts employees in fits of rage, Musk said that he only gives &#34;clear and frank feedback which may be construed as derision,&#34; according to <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2021-07-12/elon-musk-tells-court-tesla-s-solarcity-deal-wasn-t-a-bailout?sref=LspfQlRv\">Bloomberg</a>. </p><p>Tesla is notorious for its high executive turnover, and there have been <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-reportedly-terrified-tesla-staff-with-his-firing-sprees-2018-12\">reports</a> that Musk goes on wild firing rampages. Tesla has refuted those claims. </p><h2>&#34;I was offered several high-paid jobs on Wall Street.&#34;</h2><p>In another timeline, Musk <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-career-wall-street-turned-down-high-paid-jobs-2021-7\">could have worked in finance</a>, he told the court on Monday. </p><p>&#34;I was offered several high-paid jobs on Wall Street,&#34; Musk said, per Bloomberg. &#34;I declined.&#34; </p><p>Musk didn&#39;t say where he could have worked. But, with a net worth close to $200 billion, he has made out well for himself anyway. </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/s&p_500_500\">S&#38;P 500</a> has rallied sharply over the last year to hit repeated record highs - but Wall Street analysts are backing the benchmark US stock index to continue its ascent.</p><p>Industry analysts on average expect the S&#38;P 500 to rise 9.6% from Monday&#39;s closing price of 4,384.6 over the next 12 months to hit 4,803.6, according to data compiled by FactSet.</p><p>A 9.6% rise would be considerably slower than the 37% increase the S&#38;P 500 has experienced over the last 12 months. But it would nonetheless represent a solid gain at a time when some investors are questioning whether US stocks can continue their stellar rally.</p><p>FactSet, a data company which aggregates industry forecasts, said analysts expect the energy and materials sectors to see the biggest increase in stock prices. Analysts on average expect energy and materials stocks to rise 17% and 16% respectively from their closing prices on Thursday, when the data was compiled.</p><p>Both energy and materials are so-called <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-are-cyclical-stocks\">cyclical sectors</a> that are expected to benefit from the reopening of economies and stronger growth and inflation. Such sectors fared badly during the 2020 coronavirus pandemic but have rebounded in 2021.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/6-stock-strategies-secure-profits-stocks-independent-advisor-alliance-zaccarelli-2021-7\">The CIO of a $7 billion financial advisory firm details 6 strategies to secure profits no matter where stocks go - and breaks down the Fed&#39;s tightrope walk to keep the bull market roaring</a></em></p><p>Many Wall Street analysts have predicted the so-called reflation trade <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/us-stocks-outlook-value-rotation-reopening-inflation-jpmorgan-2021-6\">to continue</a>, despite the interest in cyclical stocks cooling in recent weeks. Inflation showed little sign of slowing on Tuesday, when data showed prices rose at the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/consumer-price-index-inflation-june-2021-7\">fastest rate since 2008</a> in June, at 5.4% year on year.</p><p>The BlackRock Investment Institute said in its recent mid-year outlook: &#34;We lean further into cyclicality to capture potential upside as the broadening pickup in economic activity boosts corporate earnings expectations.&#34;</p><p>However, BlackRock said it was becoming more selective about US stocks as it expects growth to peak in the coming months after the rapid rebound in the first half of the year.</p><p>Analysts at LPL Financial said in its mid-year outlook: &#34;Economic improvement should continue to support S&#38;P 500 Index earnings, which had a stunning first quarter.</p><p>&#34;While valuations remain somewhat elevated, we think they look reasonable after considering still low interest rates and earnings growth daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell</strong><strong data-stringify-type=\"bold\">.</strong></a></li>\n</ul><p>Allegations of currency-trade manipulation are bubbling up into a potential class-action suit against several big banks, according to a <a href=\"https://www.ft.com/content/2eec1003-0c95-44fb-86b3-43767c1aac10?accessToken=zwAAAXqgGNmIkc8u7BADDJVE-9OGs0N2fBqsEA.MEUCIDG6Nvg__S6XeoIsJGloOWy8blCWaghyCaAhaooA5FnpAiEAu3U86Ylqh7W7Am_smVa3ZGmel20IpzDXeFaqELlZexQ&sharetype=gift?token=ec69052a-d0e7-4769-82b4-48ebfc7ca201a201\">report</a> from the Financial Times.</p><p>Two high-powered legal teams are jostling to bring a collective action against the banks in London courts, pursuing a US-style class-action strategy that could lead to huge payouts. Under a 2015 UK law, class-action suits can be pursued if there are suspected violations of competition law in play, according to the FT.</p><p>The banks, which include UBS, Barclays, Citibank, and JPMorgan, are accused of colluding to rig prices in the $6 trillion foreign-exchange market between 2007 and 2013. Traders allegedly coordinated currency bets in online chat rooms, exchanging information on customer orders and prices. </p><p>In 2019, the banks coughed up over €1 billion in fines to the European Commission, following on similar fines paid to US, UK, and Swiss regulators. In sum, banks have paid north of $12 billion in fines over the FX-rigging scandal, according to the FT.</p><p>UBS initially escaped the 2019 European fines by disclosing its misconduct early, but the regulatory action was effectively an &#34;open invitation for parties who may have been impacted by these cartels to sue these banks,&#34; as one lawyer <a href=\"https://www.bbc.com/news/business-48292946\">told the BBC</a> at the time.</p><p>That prediction now seems prescient as the two competing class-action cases are being bankrolled by litigation financiers who buy equity in the outcome of a case.</p><p>Separately, HSBC is facing allegations from a former client of FX fraud in front of London&#39;s High Court. HSBC denies the claims.</p><p> </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/nok-stock\">Nokia</a> shares on Tuesday soared to their highest price in more than five months after the Finnish telecom equipment maker -- considered part of the so-called group of meme stocks -- told investors it may lift its financial outlook for the year.</p><p>The company said its business has continued to strengthen during the second quarter, brightening prospects for the rest of 2021. Net sales are among the metrics that may be revised later this month.</p><p>NYSE-listed Nokia climbed 11% to $5.99 and volume of nearly 69 million shares traded during the session was well ahead of average daily volume of about 38 million shares. The stock hit its highest price since January 27 when it reached $9.79 during a rally in meme stocks.</p><p>Nokia has been swept up in the meme-stock trading phenomenon spearheaded by retail investors who have also embraced <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/gme-stock\">GameStop</a> and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/amc-stock\">AMC Entertainment</a>. Traders active on Reddit&#39;s Wall Street Bets forum and other social media sites have been banding together to buy and hold onto stocks targeted by hedge funds betting on their decline.</p><p>Nokia said it&#39;s making progress with its three-phased plan outlined in March to achieve sustainable and profitable growth. </p><p>&#34;Our first-half performance has shown evidence of this in good cost control and also benefited from strength in a number of our end markets. We continue to expect some headwinds in the second half as we have previously highlighted but our performance in the first half provides a good foundation for the full year,&#34; said Pekka Lundmark, Nokia&#39;s president and CEO, in a statement.</p><p>An updated outlook from Nokia would be part of the company&#39;s July 29 release of second-quarter and half-year financial results.</p><p>In April, the company reiterated its view of net sales of €20.6 billion ($24.4 billion) to €21.8 billion and a comparable operating margin of 7%-10%. class=\"copyright\">Virgin Galactic</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Virgin Galactic is offering new shares to raise $500 million to develop its space fleet and spaceports.</li>\n<li>The CEO told the Financial Times the company faces hurdles following the successful flight with founder Richard Branson.</li>\n<li>There will be two more tests this year before commercial passenger flights begin in 2022.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Virgin Galactic is looking to raise $500 million in order to fund the development of its space fleet and expansion of its spaceports around the world, according to <a href=\"https://www.sec.gov/ix?doc=/Archives/edgar/data/1706946/000170694621000092/spce-20210712.htm\">filings</a> with the US Securities Exchange Commission.</p><p>The announcement came one day after founder Richard Branson successfully flew with a crew of company employees <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/virgin-galactic-rocket-plane-flies-richard-branson-crew-to-space-2021-7\">to the edge of space</a> in the VSS Unity space plane.</p><p>But several short-term challenges remain before the space tourism company can fully ramp up to its target of offering 400 flights per year from every spaceport, the CEO said in <a href=\"https://www.ft.com/content/0d9c9174-9374-4c48-a25b-3ae7dd6764b3?campaign_id=4&emc=edit_dk_20210713&instance_id=35187&nl=dealbook&regi_id=56750342&segment_id=63299&te=1&user_id=acfe5b76710da32397f71737e938fa015b76710da32397f71737e938fa01\">an interview with the Financial Times</a>.</p><p>&#34;I think for a while this is going to be a very supply-constrained business,&#34; said Michael Colglazier, who became CEO last year.</p><p>The company plans to complete two more test flights this year before it begins chipping away at the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/celebrities-reserve-tickets-to-fly-space-richard-branson-virgin-galactic-2021-7\">600-person waiting list</a> of commercial passenger ticket holders in 2022.</p><p>The sold tickets are worth a combined $80 million, according to filings, and another 1,000 people have placed $1,000 deposits toward the future purchase of tickets when sales reopen.</p><p>With room for just four passengers on the StarShipTwo space plane, Colglazier said Virgin Galactic plans to introduce two new craft that are easier to maintain and turnaround to support daily flights.</p><p>&#34;I&#39;m expecting high single-digit numbers to low double-digit numbers of spaceships [at each site] in order to kind of reach numbers like that,&#34; he said.</p><p>Colglazier also told the FT that the decision to move Branson&#39;s flight schedule forward - ahead of Jeff Bezos&#39; Blue Origin flight next week - was motivated not by rivalry but by Branson&#39;s role in testing the customer experience.</p><p><strong><a href=\"https://www.ft.com/content/0d9c9174-9374-4c48-a25b-3ae7dd6764b3?campaign_id=4&emc=edit_dk_20210713&instance_id=35187&nl=dealbook&regi_id=56750342&segment_id=63299&te=1&user_id=acfe5b76710da32397f71737e938fa015b76710da32397f71737e938fa01\">Read the full Financial Times story here</a>.</strong></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a
