+0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/60edb740ca74780018ae916c?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"07b763a8e559d58c9ddaeb234d6878f7","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn81@2020_4/2021/07/13/17-22-21-669_98dfb8c337f7d1f0.webp","destWidth":1536,"destHeight":1152,"sourceBytes":68628,"destBytes":68628,"author":"dreuter@insider.com (Dominick Reuter)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/60edb747ca74780018ae916d?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn44@2020_1/2021/07/13/17-22-24-974_2aa04a0aa17683ba.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn12@2020_2/2021/07/13/17-22-25-174_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=i3xfTk5kVRM:dADMesMqC1Y:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn2@2020_5/2021/07/13/17-22-25-360_6d44e5717a4951c3.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=i3xfTk5kVRM:dADMesMqC1Y:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn35@2020_4/2021/07/13/17-22-22-670_172017a050581ee0.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn83@2020_2/2021/07/13/17-22-23-761_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=i3xfTk5kVRM:dADMesMqC1Y:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn63@2020_4/2021/07/13/17-22-24-859_61230bf8a321ed0d.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/i3xfTk5kVRM":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn91@2020_4/2021/07/13/17-22-25-615_d10724128f27450e.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626196914879},{"createdTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:54","updatedTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:54","title":"The US doesn't really know how widespread the Delta variant is because its virus sequencing is lagging far behind many other rich nations","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/delta-variant-us-covid-test-sequencing-strain-cases-infections-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60ed7196ca74780018ae907e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"coronavirus test\" height=\"717\" width=\"957\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A female doctor holds a swab in one of the central fairgrounds in the outpatient corona test facility.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.gettyimages.com/detail/news-photo/april-2020-berlin-a-female-doctor-holds-a-swab-in-one-of-news-photo/1210865862?adppopup=true\" target=\"_blank\">Britta Pedersen/picture alliance via Getty Images</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li><strong>The US doesn&#39;t really know how widespread Delta is because of inadequate sequencing of tests.</strong></li>\n<li><strong>In the past six months, just 4% of all positive COVID-19 were sequenced and reported to a central database.</strong></li>\n<li><strong>The UK is at 18.6%, Singapore 46.5%, Australia 58.7%, and New Zealand 41.5%.</strong></li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The US doesn&#39;t know exactly how widespread the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/delta-variant-map-covid-risk-vaccination-rate-arkansas-nevada-missouri-2021-7\">Delta coronavirus variant is</a> because of inadequate virus sequencing. </p><p>Sequencing tells you what strain of the virus is causing a COVID-19 infection.</p><p>Data from the <a href=\"https://www.gisaid.org/index.php?id=208\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Global Initiative on Sharing All Influenza Data</a> (GISAID), a highly-regarded central genetic sequencing database, <a href=\"https://www.gisaid.org/index.php?id=208\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">showed on Tuesday</a> that in the past six months the US had sequenced and shared results for 4.12% of all positive tests.</p><p>Over the same time period, the UK had sequenced and shared 18.6% of positive tests, Singapore 46.5%, Australia 58.7%, and New Zealand 41.5%, per GISAID.</p><p>The Delta variant was detected in the US on February 5 and became the primary cause of new US infections on July 7, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/cdc-delta-variant-more-than-half-cases-us-2021-7\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">according to the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention</a> (CDC). The Delta variant now accounts for more than 80% of new cases in the US, <a href=\"https://outbreak.info/situation-reports?pango=B.1.617.2&loc=IND&loc=GBR&loc=USA&selected=USAamp;selected=USA\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">according to Scripps Research&#39;s Outbreak.info,</a> which is backed by the CDC and uses GISAID data.  </p><p><a href=\"https://outbreak.info/situation-reports/caveats\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Outbreak.info</a> said on its website that the sequencing data it provides is a &#34;best estimate&#34; because the tests sequenced and shared to GISAID don&#39;t always represent an average American. For example, they often come from an outbreak, a breakthrough infection from <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fully-vaccinated-people-got-covid-after-an-outdoor-wedding-2021-7\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">someone who&#39;s vaccinated,</a> a patient with unusually severe disease, or those with a travel history.</p><p><strong><em>Read more:</em></strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/vaccine-mrna-covid-drug-treatment-future-of-medicine-2021-5\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>Experts explain why the mRNA tech that revolutionized COVID-19 vaccines could be the answer to incurable diseases, heart attacks, and even snake bites: &#39;The possibilities are endless&#39;</em></a></p><p>This could lead to overestimates of the number of infections caused by variants such as Delta, Outbreak.info said.</p><p>The CDC said in January that it had partnered with commercial labs and academic institutions to try to sequence <a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/coronavirus/2019-ncov/variants/cdc-role-surveillance.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">up to 20,000 samples a week,</a> which would have amounted to 18.4% of the US&#39;s weekly cases on Tuesday. The GISAID data suggests it is far short of this goal.</p><p>The same GISAID data showed that it took the US an average of 22 days to upload sequencing data onto its database, which could mean estimates for the number of Delta infections are outdated. The UK took an average of 11 days.</p><p>The US was not lagging behind every rich nation: it&#39;s 4.12% rate of positive tests sequenced and shared was higher than Israel&#39;s, at 1.26%.</p><p>A modeling study <a href=\"https://www.medrxiv.org/content/10.1101/2021.01.12.21249613v1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">posted in January </a>estimated that a country needed to sequence 5% of positive tests to detect an emerging strain, assuming 0.1% to 1% of the population were infected with it.  </p><p>The CDC <a href=\"https://www.ft.com/content/f8e83ce5-037f-469d-bee9-aaa37f6e2554\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">told the Financial Times</a> that it was &#34;confident&#34; that with the current surveillance strategy &#34;new and emerging variants would be detected well before they become prominent.&#34; </p><h2>Patchwork approach to sequencing</h2><p>Will Lee, vice-president of science at the genomics company Helix, which has a sequencing contract with the CDC, said that piecing data together was a challenge. &#34;With so many different places and means of getting tested, it can be hard to get the sequences,&#34; Lee<a href=\"https://www.ft.com/content/f8e83ce5-037f-469d-bee9-aaa37f6e2554\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> told the FT.</a></p><p>Bronwyn MacInnis, director of pathogen genomic surveillance at MIT and Harvard&#39;s Broad Institute, said that the biggest barrier to &#34;closing the gap&#34; with other countries was getting positive tests to sites to be sequenced, per <a href=\"https://www.ft.com/content/f8e83ce5-037f-469d-bee9-aaa37f6e2554\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">the FT</a>. </p><p>Thomas Friedrich, professor of pathobiological sciences at the University of Wisconsin-Madison, told <a href=\"https://www.ft.com/content/f8e83ce5-037f-469d-bee9-aaa37f6e2554\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">the FT</a> that federal regulations designed to protect people&#39;s privacy can get in the way of the &#34;rapid sharing of information we need.&#34; States interpret these regulations in different ways, he said.</p><p>Oklahoma has sequenced 736 positive tests, whereas Texas has sequenced more than 59,000, according to <a href=\"https://outbreak.info/situation-reports/caveats\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Scripp&#39;s </a>Outbreak.info.</p><div in 2021.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Photo by Spencer Platt/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The S&#38;P 500 index is on track for the most record closing highs 39 closing highs. </li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Investors have been propelling the S&#38;P 500 index to a string of record highs this year, driving the broad stock-market measure toward its best run in more than 25 years, according to Bespoke Investment Group. </p><p>The index, valued at roughly $36 trillion, has notched 39 closing highs <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/stocks-market-news-us-record-highs-earnings-season-growth-dow-2021-7\">through Monday&#39;s session</a>, which was made possible by overcoming a modest intraday loss. The <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/dow_jones?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestm=ingest\">Dow Jones Industrial Average</a> and the <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/nasdaq_composite?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestm=ingest\">Nasdaq Composite</a> also started the week by logging closing highs.</p><p>The S&#38;P 500 at its current pace is headed toward 74 record highs on a closing basis for 2021, which would rank as the second-most of all time, Bespoke said. In 1995, there were 77 closing highs. Monday&#39;s win left the index with 10 record closes in the past 12 trading sessions &#34;which is relatively uncommon over the last 50+ years,&#34; said Bespoke in a note published early Tuesday.</p><p>&#34;Like home runs coming off the bat of Pete Alonso in last night&#39;s Home Run Derby, the S&#38;P 500 is racking up record highs at an incredible pace lately,&#34; said Paul Hickey, co-founder of Bespoke Investment. The Mets&#39; first baseman Monday night in Denver slammed 23 hits to win <a href=\"https://www.espn.com/mlb/story/_/id/31808914/new-york-mets-pete-alonso-beats-baltimore-orioles-trey-mancini-final-round-repeat-home-run-derby-champion\">his second consecutive home-run derby</a>.</p><p>The S&#38;P 500 has jumped by nearly 17% this year, a performance that&#39;s been &#34;entirely driven&#34; by rising corporate earnings estimates of 21%, BofA said in a research note Monday. The firm, however, cautioned that big earnings beats for the second quarter <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/stock-market-outlook-sp500-2q-earnings-bofa-economic-growth-2021-7\">doesn&#39;t guarantee gains for strong market returns</a>. </p><p>In 1964, the broad index racked up 64 record closing highs and there were 62 in 2017.</p><p>&#34;One caveat here is that, as the last two weeks have shown, new highs tend to come in bunches, but if the S&#38;P 500 experiences a pullback, the rapid pace will dry up quickly,&#34; said Hickey. &#34;Wherever the 2021 total winds up, the pace so far this year has been impressive, to say the least.&#34;</p><div The reading marked the largest one-month change since June 2008.</p><p>On a year-over-year basis, prices increased 5.4%, higher than economists&#39; expectations for a 4.9% year-over-year increase. However, June 2020 was the lowest point for Core CPI during the pandemic shutdown, so year-over-year increases are expected. </p><p>&#34;A white-hot June CPI print has the markets jittery this morning. Stripping away food and energy, it was the highest print for Core CPI since November 1991 on a year-over-year basis, however moving forward we expect these inflation numbers to begin to cool,&#34; said Cliff Hodge, Cornerstone Wealth chief investment officer.</p><p><strong>Here&#39;s where US indexes stood at the 9:30 a.m. ET open on Tuesday:</strong></p><ul><li aria-level=\"1\"><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/s&p_500?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestm=ingest\"><strong>S&#38;P 500</strong></a><strong>:</strong> 4,379.21, down 0.12%</li><li aria-level=\"1\"><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/dow_jones?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\"><strong>Dow Jones industrial average</strong></a><strong>: </strong>34,970.62, down 0.07% (25.56 points)</li><li aria-level=\"1\"><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/nasdaq_composite?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\"><strong>Nasdaq composite</strong></a><strong style=\"color: #222222;\">: </strong>14,726.58, down 0.03%</li></ul><p>Bank earnings began this morning, with <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/jpmorgan-q2-earnings-eps-revenue-loan-losses-investment-banking-reopening-2021-7\">JPMorgan beating expectations</a> as the banking giant benefited from record investment-banking fees and the release of cash set aside to cover loan losses.</p><p><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/goldman-sachs-earnings-2q-stock-price-gs-investment-banking-2021-7\">Goldman Sachs also handily exceeded</a> analysts&#39; estimates. Investment banking generated its second highest quarterly net revenues ever, just behind the first quarter of 2021, thanks in large part to a robust IPO market. The strong numbers in that segment offset a slowdown in Goldman&#39;s trading business. </p><p>Although CPI came in higher than expected, a June <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/global-fund-manager-survey-bofa-inflation-economic-boom-2021-7\">Bank of America survey</a> reveals most fund managers believe the global economy has reached &#34;Peak Boom.&#34; Month on month, 2% fewer respondents to the bank&#39;s monthly global fund manager survey believe economic growth and inflation will rise above current predictions. Overall, 74% of fund managers still expect growth and inflation to be &#34;above trend.&#34;</p><p>The yield on the US 10-year Treasury gained 1.5 basis points to 1.378%.</p><p><a href=\"https://tripadvisor.mediaroom.com/2021-04-20-Travel-is-Heating-Up-Two-Thirds-of-Americans-Planning-Summer-Vacations\">hitting the road and traveling again</a>. </p><p>According to the <a src=\"https://i.insider.com/60ed9ba0ca74780018ae90ca?format=jpeg\" alt=\"carnival cruise\" height=\"1333\" width=\"1778\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Carnival Cruise Line&#39;s Carnival Ecstacy cruise Cruise Line</a> will soon be required to pay for travel insurance, making the cruising experience that much more <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/royal-caribbean-cruise-florida-july-different-unvaccinated-passengers-2021-7\">expensive for those who don&#39;t want the COVID-19 vaccine</a>. </p><p>Carnival will begin asking unvaccinated passengers for proof of travel insurance starting July 31, the cruise line said on its <a href=\"https://www.carnival.com/legal/covid-19-legal-notices/covid-19-guest-protocols\">website</a>. The insurance is required to cover a minimum of $10,000 in medical expenses and $30,000 in &#34;emergency medical evacuation and without COVID-19 exclusions&#34; per passenger.</p><p>Guests who are unvaccinated and don&#39;t show proof of the insurance will not be allowed to cruise and will not receive a refund. For now, children 12-years-old or younger are exempt from this policy. </p><p>&#34;Consistent with the practices of other lines who are also restarting their operations, and in the best interests of our guests who are unvaccinated, this is important coverage to have should they encounter a medical situation during their cruise,&#34; Carnival spokesperson Vance Gulliksen told <a href=\"https://www.usatoday.com/story/travel/cruises/2021/07/09/carnival-cruise-line-requiring-unvaccinated-cruisers-buy-travel-insurance/7914723002/\">USA Today&#39;s</a> Morgan Hines. </p><p>Unlike their vaccinated counterparts, unvaccinated <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/carnival-cruise-cabin-room-photos-2021-7\">Carnival guests</a> must also undergo additional COVID-19 tests. This, plus other health protocols, will amount to an extra $150 out-of-pocket charge per unvaccinated passenger.</p><p>Late last month, Royal Caribbean also announced it would <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/royal-caribbean-florida-cruise-unvaccinated-travel-insurance-2021-6\">make travel insurance mandatory</a> for unvaccinated passengers 12-years-old or older beginning August 1, a decision that came a week after <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/royal-caribbean-cruise-covid-bahamas-passengers-test-positive-2021-6\">two unvaccinated teenagers tested positive</a> for COVID-19 aboard one of the cruise line&#39;s &#34;fully vaccinated&#34; ships.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a class=\"copyright\">Alex Wong</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Bitcoin has seen outflows in Europe but inflows from North America in the latest week, according to CoinShares.</li>\n<li>Trading volumes totalled $1.58 billion for the week to July 9, the lowest since October.</li>\n<li>Multi-asset investment products, like the Bitwise 10 crypto index fund, were up here for our daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell</strong></a><strong>.</strong></li>\n</ul><p>Cryptocurrency trading volumes fell to their lowest in nine months in the latest week, as bitcoin continued to fluctuate in a relatively narrow range, according to data from digital asset manager CoinShares on Tuesday.</p><p>Outflows picked up speed in Europe, where regulators have toughened their scrutiny of cryptocurrency trading in general, while US investors were net buyers of crypto assets, according to <a href=\"https://coinshares.com/research/digital-asset-fund-flows\">CoinShares</a> data. </p><p>The crypto trading volumes totalled $1.58 billion for the week, as activity quietened mostly for bitcoin. Bitcoin saw net outflows of $6.9 million, a steep decline from net inflows of $38.9 million the week before. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60e4474093b49f0018ee088a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Weekly crypto asset flows\" height=\"542\" width=\"785\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Weekly crypto asset flows\n<p class=\"copyright\">CoinShares</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>&#34;In recent weeks, there has been a regional divide in bitcoin inflows, with North American providers seeing consistent inflows while their European counterparts have continued to see outflows, suggesting a geographic divergence in sentiment,&#34; the report said. </p><p>So far this month, bitcoin has traded in a relatively narrow band, between lows of around $32,100 and a high of around $34,500 - a far cry from the extreme volatility of May, when it swung from a low of $30,000 to a high of nearly $59,600, according to Coinbase. </p><p>Since hitting a record of nearly $65,000 in April the coin has tumbled by nearly 50%, although it is still up almost 260% in the last year.</p><p>Regulation was another factor. The UK regulator <a href=\"https://www.fca.org.uk/news/press-releases/fca-bans-sale-crypto-derivatives-retail-consumers\">banned </a>retail consumers from buying crypto derivatives last year. Since then, it <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/binance-uk-ban-mean-local-investors-regular-trading-cryptocurrencies-fca-2021-6\">ordered</a> Binance, a crypto exchange, to halt regulated activities in the country. </p><p>&#34;Europe is a little bit behind in terms of investment into crypto assets,&#34; James Butterfill, CoinShares chief investment strategist, told Insider. </p><p>CoinShares is Europe&#39;s largest crypto asset manager. The company had $3.35 billion under management by the end of the first quarter, according to its recent earnings report.</p><p>Other crypto assets witnessed net inflows. Ether saw inflows of $800,000, Binance coin saw inflows of $400,000  and cardano&#39;s ada token saw $600,000 in flows. </p><p>Multi-asset investment products, like Bitwise 10 crypto index fund, which tracks the performance of the top 10 crypto coins for example, were the most popular last week, with inflows of $1.2 million. CoinShares said this suggested investors were diversifying their holdings.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 01:21:54","updatedTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:54","title":"The Delta variant is hitting red states hardest as the US's vaccine divide widens","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/delta-coronavirus-variant-hitting-republican-states-vaccine-divide-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60ecab12ca74780018ae8f81?format=jpeg\" alt=\"anti vaccine trump rally\" height=\"2333\" width=\"3500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A protester holds an anti-vaccine sign as supporters of President Donald Trump rally in Woodland Hills, California, on May 16, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">David McNew/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The Delta variant is sickening people most in unvaccinated, heavily Republican &#34;red&#34; states.</li>\n<li>Arkansas, Mississippi, Missouri, and Wyoming have seen upticks in cases and hospitalizations.</li>\n<li>But the variant has had little effect in blue states like Maine, New Hampshire, and Vermont.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The US&#39;s daily coronavirus cases have soared 60% in the last two weeks as the Delta variant strengthens its hold on the country. Delta now accounts for more than half of US cases, making it the dominant strain nationwide.</p><p>But the variant isn&#39;t hitting all states equally. Delta cases have risen primarily in states with low vaccination rates, which for the most part are heavily Republican - &#34;red&#34; states like Arkansas, Mississippi, Missouri, and Wyoming. Overall, these states have seen higher upticks in daily cases and hospitalizations than &#34;blue&#34; states that voted Democratic in the 2020 election.</p><p>In Missouri, for instance, daily cases have risen around 75% in the last two weeks, from around 800 to 1,400 cases per day. Hospitalizations have also risen 34% during that time, from around 830 to 1,100 per day. Delta has made up nearly 70% of all coronavirus cases there over the last two months, according to data compiled by Scripps Research&#39;s <a href=\"https://outbreak.info/about\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"77c58785ec6d76f4e89b3038cc587802\">Outbreak.info tracker</a>. Less than half of Missouri residents (around 46%) have received at least one vaccine dose so far - well below the US average of 56%.</p><p>But Vermont, where <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/vermont-to-be-first-state-to-reach-herd-immunity-2021-7\">nearly 75% of residents have received at least one dose</a>, has reported just five daily cases and five daily hospitalizations in the last two weeks. Delta made up less than 1% of coronavirus cases there in the last two months.</p><p>Other blue states, like Maine, New Hampshire, and Pennsylvania, have also reported some of the lowest case numbers and highest vaccination rates in the country. In each of these states, Delta has represented less than 10% of overall cases in the last two months, according to <a href=\"https://outbreak.info/about\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"77c58785ec6d76f4e89b3038cc587802\">Outbreak.info</a>.</p><p>&#34;We&#39;ve got to get away from the divisiveness,&#34; Anthony Fauci, director of the National Institute of Allergy and Infectious Disease, <a href=\"https://abcnews.go.com/Politics/fauci-urges-people-put-politics-vaccinated-nasty-delta/story?id=78774860\">told ABC</a> on Sunday - a reference to the way the US&#39;s vaccine divide falls along political lines.</p><p>Viruses, Fauci added, &#34;don&#39;t know the difference between a Democrat, a Republican, or an Independent.&#34;</p><h2>Republicans are less likely than Democrats to trust vaccines</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60e4d4d4102fd50018478031?format=jpeg\" alt=\"vermont covid-19 vaccine\" height=\"4024\" width=\"6048\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A National Guard soldier gives a COVID-19 vaccine at a pop-up vaccination stand at the Vermont Creamery in Websterville, Vermont, on June 29, 2021.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Ed Jones/AFP/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Data <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/06/28/briefing/covid-cases-rising-red-america.html\">collected by the New York Times</a> shows that just 34% of people are fully vaccinated in an average US county that voted for Donald Trump, whereas 45% of people are fully vaccinated in an average county that voted for Joe Biden.</p><p>There are several reasons why vaccination rates are stalling in red states. For one, Republicans are more likely to believe that vaccines aren&#39;t safe or that the shots aren&#39;t necessary to protect their health, according to <a href=\"https://www.kff.org/coronavirus-covid-19/poll-finding/kff-covid-19-vaccine-monitor-june-2021/\">a June survey</a> from the Kaiser Family Foundation.</p><p>Additionally, Republican states also tend to be more rural, so access to shots may still prevent some people in those areas from getting immunized.</p><p>In Arkansas, for instance, around 42% of counties are rural. Research from Boston Children&#39;s Hospital suggests that <a href=\"https://vaccineplanner.org/\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"a9a1f7d463a4a9339b3daca9473eabc1\">several Arkansas counties</a> qualify as &#34;vaccine deserts,&#34; with the nearest COVID-19 vaccination site more than a 15-minute drive away. Just 43% of Arkansas residents have received at least one vaccine dose.</p><p>But the state&#39;s health director, Dr. José Romero, blames the low vaccination rate on widespread vaccine hesitancy - not lack of access. The Kaiser Family Foundation <a href=\"https://www.kff.org/coronavirus-covid-19/poll-finding/kff-covid-19-vaccine-monitor-june-2021/\">survey</a> found that rural residents are also significantly more vaccine hesitant than urban or suburban residents.</p><p>&#34;We&#39;ve done everything we can,&#34; Romero <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/arkansas-delta-variant-epicenter-vaccine-uptake-low-2021-7\">told Insider</a>. &#34;We&#39;ve made the vaccine available. We&#39;ve gone the extra mile to make it pretty much on demand if you want it.&#34;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60e860386164f3001853b782?format=jpeg\" alt=\"arkansas vaccine campaign\" height=\"2000\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Arkansas Gov. Asa Hutchinson watches an ad featuring former NBA star Sidney Moncrief that encourages people to get the COVID-19 vaccine, at the state capitol in Little Rock on May 20, 2021.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Andrew Demillo/AP Photo</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Delta has made up nearly 40% of Arkansas&#39; cases over the last two months - among the highest shares in the country. Romero said he has tried to remind residents that the variant poses &#34;a much greater threat&#34; than the original coronavirus strain.</p><p>An analysis from Public Health England <a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/news/confirmed-cases-of-covid-19-variants-identified-in-uk\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"dd1b792187543a6018d531a068650246\">found</a> that Delta was associated with a 60% increased risk of household transmission relative to the Alpha variant discovered in the UK, though <a href=\"https://assets.publishing.service.gov.uk/government/uploads/system/uploads/attachment_data/file/997418/Variants_of_Concern_VOC_Technical_Briefing_17.pdf\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"456757ef415b613b6bac4f8af9a3f800\">more recent estimates</a> suggest the difference is closer to 40%. The Alpha variant is already about <a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/mmwr/volumes/70/wr/mm7003e2.htm\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"25c005816586d51abf3ac760485238c9\">50% more transmissible</a> than the original strain, according to the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention.</p><p>Researchers in Scotland also found that getting infected with the Delta variant <a href=\"https://www.thelancet.com/journals/lancet/article/PIIS0140-6736(21)01358-1/fulltext\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"744749b438117a8ea8419d175d9b37e2\">doubled the risk</a> of hospital admission relative to Alpha. (Previous studies have <a href=\"https://assets.publishing.service.gov.uk/government/uploads/system/uploads/attachment_data/file/982640/Feb_NERVTAG_update_note_on_B.1.1.7_severity.pdf\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"683c672c4592a0c551f6fa4c64383b02\">suggested</a> that the Alpha variant may be 30% to 70% deadlier than the original strain.)</p><p>Vaccines, of course, significantly lower that risk, but it&#39;s important to complete the full course. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-well-does-one-vaccine-dose-work-delta-variant-coronavirus-2021-7\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"81563953dc01d85faccd2b7f6353bdb4\">New research</a> suggests that partially vaccinated people are more vulnerable to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/covid-19-delta-variant-symptoms-headache-runny-nose-sore-throat-2021-6\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"f0a1b2d290c36e29ab5caf53445f3434\">symptomatic Delta infections</a> than they might be to other strains. A <a href=\"https://www.nature.com/articles/s41586-021-03777-9\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-ml-dynamic=\"true\" data-ml-dynamic-type=\"sl\" data-orig-url=\"https://www.nature.com/articles/s41586-021-03777-9\" data-ml-id=\"4\" data-ml=\"true\" data-xid=\"fr1625839464788hbi\" data-skimlinks-tracking=\"\" data-uri=\"c94edd2d51fdfc6d27802c6bb053ca3d\">study</a> published last week in the journal Nature found that a single dose of Pfizer&#39;s vaccine was either weakly or not at all effective against the variant.</p><p>&#34;It&#39;s very clear that this is a nasty variant,&#34; Fauci <a href=\"https://abcnews.go.com/Politics/fauci-urges-people-put-politics-vaccinated-nasty-delta/story?id=78774860\">told ABC</a>. &#34;It has a much greater capability of transmitting from person to person.&#34; </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/delta-coronavirus-variant-hitting-republican-states-vaccine-divide-2021-7'>Business Insider</a></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=hbQt35CVaiY:8WtKuJr1-uA:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img Alone Can Fix It&#34; about Trump&#39;s last year in office was published Tuesday.</li>\n<li>Giuliani wanted to tell Trump he had won several states before it was possible to tell, it said.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Rudy Giuliani urged those around President Donald Trump on election night 2020 to tell the president he had won states he had not, according to a new book. </p><p>The claim came in an excerpt of &#34;I Alone Can Fix It: Donald J Trump&#39;s Catastrophic Final Year&#34; by  Carol D. Leonnig and Philip Rucker of The Washington Post.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2021/07/13/book-excerpt-i-alone-can-fix-it/\">The excerpt was published Tuesday by The Post.</a> It follows numerous Trumpworld figures on the night of the 2020 election, including Giuliani.</p><p>It says the former New York mayor urged Trump aides to tell him he&#39;d won states long before they were possible to call. He gave the advice for Pennsylvania and Michigan, it says, which ultimately were called for Joe Biden.</p><p>Lennig and Rucker wrote that Giuliani had his own &#34;war room&#34; set up in the White House&#39;s Red Room, separate to the two others Trump had arranged.</p><p>As results came in, he began to &#34;cause a commotion,&#34; trying to get into the private quarters where Trump was, they said. </p><p>It recounts campaign manager Bill Stepien, White House Chief of Staff Mark Meadows and senior campaign manager Jason Miller taking Giuliani aside as others speculated that he had been drinking too much.</p><p>Giuliani, the book says, went through the projections state by state, asking the three what was happening. &#34;What&#39;s happening in Michigan?&#34; he is reported to have asked.</p><p data-el=\"text\">When Stepien, Meadows and Miller told him each time that it was too early to say, Giuliani is quoted as saying: &#34;Just say we won.&#34;</p><p data-el=\"text\">He gave the same advice for Pennsylvania, the book said, and kept going &#34;state after state,&#34; though the excerpt did not specify which.</p><p data-el=\"text\">Early results gave Trump a lead in Pennsylvania, which evaporated over time as later returns favored Biden. Many networks, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/joe-biden-wins-general-election-against-donald-trump-2020-11\">including Insider, called the entire election for Biden</a> once they were confident that Trump had no way of regaining his lead in that Pennsylvania.</p><p data-el=\"text\">Giuliani&#39;s predictions of victory were &#34;based on nothing,&#34; the book said. </p><p data-el=\"text\">According to the excerpt, Meadows said: &#34;We can&#39;t do that.&#34;</p><p data-el=\"text\">In the end, Trump did not need convincing of the falsehood anyway. He had long trailed the false idea that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-was-convinced-election-night-would-repeat-of-2016-report-2020-11\">his victory was inevitable</a> unless election fraud was involved - a notion that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-mail-in-voting-end-for-republicans-2020-5\">he had spent months sowing</a>.</p><p data-el=\"text\">He brought it up again on election night, after Fox News called Arizona for Biden. An apoplectic Trump <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-falsely-claims-he-won-presidential-election-2020-10\">announced that the election was being stolen from him</a>, famously saying: &#34;Frankly, we did win this election.&#34;</p><p data-el=\"text\">Giuliani did not immediately respond to Insider&#39;s request for comment. </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original Adam Kinzinger, a US Air Force veteran who flew missions in Afghanistan, in a tweet said, &#34;This is horrible-yet it&#39;s the reality of announcing the U.S. withdrawal from Afghanistan. Removing the peacekeepers and leaving the Afghan people without support is a grave mistake, Mr. President.&#34;</p><p>Senate Minority Leader Mitch McConnell on Tuesday called Biden&#39;s Afghanistan withdrawal a &#34;global embarrassment.&#34;</p><p>The incident took place on June 16 in the town of Dawlat Abad in Faryab province, which is close to Afghanistan&#39;s border with Turkeministan. The Taliban dismissed the video as a fabrication. But the Red Cross confirmed that 22 bodies were retrieved, and CNN spoke with witnesses and verified several videos of the incident.  </p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">-The Lead CNN  (@TheLeadCNN) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1414738632733335553?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">July 13, 2021</a></blockquote><script async=\"\" src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p> </p><p>The withdrawal of American troops from Afghanistan - set to be complete by the end of August - marks an end to the longest conflict in US history. But the US pullout does not mean an end to violent conflict in Afghanistan, which has seen consistent fighting for roughly four decades. The Taliban last week said it&#39;s taken over <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/world/asia-pacific/militia-commanders-rush-aid-afghan-forces-against-taliban-2021-07-09/\">85% of the country</a>, and with regional militias popping up across Afghanistan there are worries that the war will escalate after the US departure.  </p><p>&#34;Civil war is certainly a path that can be visualized if it continues on the trajectory it&#39;s on,&#34; Gen. Austin S. Miller, who <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/top-us-general-afghanistan-austin-s-miller-is-stepping-down-2021-7\">stepped down</a> as the top US commander in Afghanistan on Monday, <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/06/29/world/asia/afghanistan-civil-war-miller.html\">said earlier this month</a>. </p><p>Biden announced the plan to withdraw troops in April, and has <a href=\"https://www.whitehouse.gov/briefing-room/speeches-remarks/2021/07/08/remarks-by-president-biden-on-the-drawdown-of-u-s-forces-in-afghanistan/\">fervently defended the move</a> amid escalating concerns about the future of Afghanistan with the US departure nearly complete. Proponents of Biden&#39;s withdrawal contend that the pullout was long overdue, making the case that the costs of staying in Afghanistan far outweigh the benefits.</p><p>&#34;Let me ask those who wanted us to stay: How many more - how many thousands more of America&#39;s daughters and sons are you willing to risk? How long would you have them stay?&#34; Biden said in a speech last Thursday.</p><p>But critics have characterized the withdrawal as a hasty retreat that endangers local populations - <a href=\"https://www.defenseone.com/policy/2021/04/biden-must-protect-womens-rights-after-afghanistan-withdrawal/173657/\">especially women</a> - and effectively hands the country over to the Taliban.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">-Jennifer Jacobs  (@JenniferJJacobs) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1414958542172434446?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">July 13, 2021</a></blockquote><script async=\"\" src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" military, who is better trained, better equipped and more competent in terms of conducting war,&#34; <a href=\"https://twitter.com/CBSNews/status/1413202883156271110?s=20\">the president said</a> on 01:21:54","updatedTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:54","title":"I'm a teacher in a tiny Alaskan village. My class consists of 8 students and there are no sports teams or after-school clubs - here's what my life is like.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-life-like-teacher-alaskan-bush-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60ec4c38ca74780018ae8d70?format=jpeg\" alt=\"two small white buildings in the Alaskan bush\" height=\"2160\" width=\"2880\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The view of Taryn Williams&#39; house, right, from the school steps.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Taryn Williams</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Taryn Williams, 28, is a teacher and freelance writer based in the rural Alaskan Bush.</li>\n<li>Everything is really close by, but groceries cost more than they do in mainland US.</li>\n<li>She spends an hour cooking dinner and stays entertained by participating in local customs.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>One of the greatest benefits of life in the Alaskan Bush is how close everything is. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60ec4da3ca74780018ae8d83?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Taryn Williams\" height=\"576\" width=\"768\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Taryn Williams.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Taryn Williams</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>When I lived in Philadelphia, it took me nearly an hour to commute to my school via public transportation. <p>Here, it takes less than two minutes to walk there. I get to sleep in later and have a slower morning, as there&#39;s no stress that I&#39;ll have to pay for a taxi if I miss the train.</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moved-alaskan-bush-teacher-expensive-love-it-2021-6\" data-e2e-name=\"inline-read-more-link\">I moved from Atlanta to a tiny Alaskan village of 270 people. It&#39;s wildly expensive, but I&#39;ve never felt more at home.</a></em></p><p>There are no coffee shops on my route (or any in a hundred-mile radius). Instead, I make my own chai lattes with chai tea, milk, cinnamon, and spices in a pot on the stove. It&#39;s not quite as convenient as a local shop, but it tastes just as good.</p><p>School is different in the Bush, too. Most teachers have multigrade classrooms (think kindergarten to fourth grade or all of middle and high school) and class sizes are generally smaller.</p><h2><strong>In my current seventh- to twelfth-grade class, I teach 8 students in 5 subjects.</strong> </h2><p>With students in so many different grade levels, there&#39;s a lot more facilitating than there is in larger schools, but my students have also gained an enormous amount of independence because of this.</p><p>Since I live so close to school, I&#39;m able to go home for lunch every day, and it&#39;s something I&#39;ve really grown to appreciate.</p><p>Last year, my students brought me a puppy they found - there&#39;s a problem with puppy overpopulation in the Bush - and she&#39;s been with me ever since. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60ec4ca1ca74780018ae8d77?format=jpeg\" alt=\"white puppy on a mountain in the Alaskan bush\" height=\"609\" width=\"812\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Taryn Williams&#39; dog, Betty.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kyle Comeau</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>My lunch is only 30 minutes, but my house is close enough that I can get there quickly and play with her outside for a few minutes while my food heats up.</p><h2><strong>There are no local sports clubs students can join, and they can only interact with youth from other places remotely.</strong></h2><p>I want my students to have the most enjoyable high school experience possible, so I&#39;m always looking for after-school opportunities for them.</p><p>Most recently, I facilitated an internship where students learned how to make their own podcast from a <a href=\"https://podcasts.apple.com/us/podcast/on-the-land/id1494806427\">Native Alaskan podcaster</a>. I try to find activities that align with my students&#39; interests and guide my search based on that.</p><h2><strong>There are no restaurants, movie theaters, bowling alleys, or other &#39;traditional&#39; Western sources of entertainment.</strong> </h2><p>My students often ask me to take walks with them or share a mug of tea after school. They enjoy learning about the other places I&#39;ve lived and what my life was like where I grew up. Often, they accompany me when I take my puppy for a walk down to the local store and post office. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60ec4cfdca74780018ae8d7c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"a scenic view of the Alaskan bush\" height=\"2160\" width=\"2880\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The view of the village from outside Taryn Williams&#39; home.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Taryn Williams</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h2><strong>The store is small and the prices are higher than you would find elsewhere.</strong></h2><p>If there&#39;s something that I use frequently - something that others would use as well - they&#39;ll sometimes order it. I usually buy all perishable products there, such as pints of Ben &#38; Jerry&#39;s ($9) and blocks of cheese ($15). I buy orange juice only on special occasions, as it usually costs about $17.</p><p>After walking to the store to pick up any groceries or packages, I try to go for a longer hike or run with the puppy.</p><p>In the spring and fall, when we have 18 hours of daylight, I try to spend as much time outside as possible. In the winter, we only have a few hours of sun and I tend to stay closer to home - or follow along with <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/user/yogawithadriene\">Yoga with Adriene</a> videos on my SmartBoard at school.</p><h2><strong>I usually spend about an hour cooking dinner each night. </strong></h2><p>I&#39;m a vegetarian and order produce from <a href=\"https://www.fullcircle.com/\">Full Circle Farm</a> in Washington for all of my meals.</p><p>Cooking is one of my greatest joys in life and I&#39;m so grateful to live somewhere where I can dedicate significant time to it each day.</p><p>If there&#39;s something going on in town - a gathering for a wedding or a holiday, for example - I always head there and participate in local customs. Most nights, however, I cozy up in my reading nook or play a movie I downloaded on Netflix.</p><p>I often spend weekends tagging along on hunting or fishing trips even though I don&#39;t participate, and I&#39;m incredibly grateful to the villagers that have welcomed me into their lives. I&#39;ll take the things I learned from them and from living here with me wherever I go next.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 01:21:54","updatedTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:54","title":"Trump was desperate to beat Joe Biden and said on Election Day that 'I can't lose to this f------ guy,\" new book says","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-biden-i-cant-lose-to-this-fucking-guy-book-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60e9a52eca74780018ae8bef?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Donald Trump\" height=\"1337\" width=\"2674\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Former President Donald Trump speaks at a rally at the Lorain County Fairgrounds in Wellington, Ohio on June 26, 2021.\n<p class=\"copyright\">AP Photo/Tony Dejak</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Trump told aides on Election Day, &#34;I can&#39;t lose to this f------ guy,&#34; a new book said.</li>\n<li>He later added that &#34;winning is easy. Losing is never easy. Not for me it&#39;s not.&#34;</li>\n<li>Biden ended up defeating Trump in a landslide, securing 306 electoral votes compared to Trump&#39;s 232.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Former President Donald Trump was desperate to beat then-Democratic presidential candidate Joe Biden in the 2020 election, telling aides, &#34;I can&#39;t lose to this f------ guy,&#34; according to a new book excerpt <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2021/07/13/book-excerpt-i-alone-can-fix-it/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">published in The Washington Post</a>.</p><p>In &#34;<a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Alone-Can-Fix-Donald-Catastrophic/dp/0593298942\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">I Alone Can Fix It: Donald J. Trump&#39;s Catastrophic Final Year</a>,&#34; The Post&#39;s Carol Leonnig and Philip Rucker wrote that by the morning of Election Day last year, Trump was &#34;upbeat&#34; and that some of his advisors were already saying he would beat Biden in a landslide.</p><p>&#34;Several women who worked in the White House arrived wearing red sweaters in a show of optimism, while some Secret Service agents on the president&#39;s detail sported red ties for the occasion,&#34; the excerpt said.</p><p>And while Trump was exhausted from a final spurt of rallies before the big day, he was confident he had secured his victory against Biden, even as his campaign manager urged patience given the huge number of mail-in ballots that would take longer to be counted.</p><p>Later, Trump told reporters he hadn&#39;t thought about writing an acceptance speech or a concession speech.</p><p>&#34;Hopefully, we&#39;ll be only doing one of those two,&#34; he said, according to the excerpt. &#34;And, you know, winning is easy. Losing is never easy. Not for me it&#39;s not.&#34;</p><p>In the end, Biden defeated Trump in a landslide, securing 306 Electoral College votes compared to Trump&#39;s 232. A candidate needs 270 to win the White House.</p><p>Biden beat Trump in every battleground states, including Michigan, Wisconsin, Pennsylvania, Arizona, and Nevada. He also flipped Georgia, which hadn&#39;t voted for a Democrat in a presidential election since 1992, when Bill Clinton carried the state.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on process","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/sec-spacs-banks-conflicts-of-interest-deals-blacnk-check-company-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60ed973361b8600019f16c4f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"The headquarters of the U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) are seen in Washington, July 6, 2009. REUTERS/Jim Bourg\" height=\"400\" width=\"800\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The headquarters of the U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission are seen in Washington\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomson Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The SEC is investigating banks over conflicts of interest in the SPAC deal-making process, Reuters first reported. </li>\n<li>In particular, the regulator is looking into instances of banks acting as underwriter and adviser on the same deal.</li>\n<li>The SEC has requested information from top SPAC underwriters including Morgan Stanley and Goldman Sachs. </li>\n<li><a href=\"https://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/10-things-opening-bell?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\"><strong>Sign up here for our daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell</strong></a><strong>.</strong></li>\n</ul><p>The US Securities and Exchange Commission is investigating major banks over conflicts of interest in the SPAC deal-making process that exploded in the past year, <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/usa-sec-spac/refile-exclusive-u-s-sec-focuses-on-bank-fee-conflicts-as-it-steps-up-spac-inquiry-sources-idUSL2N2O90D0\">Reuters</a> first reported. </p><p>In particular, the regulator is looking into instances wherein the banks acted both as the underwriters and the advisers on the same SPAC deal and whether certain fee structures may have incentivized underwriters to secure unsuitable mergers, sources told <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/usa-sec-spac/refile-exclusive-u-s-sec-focuses-on-bank-fee-conflicts-as-it-steps-up-spac-inquiry-sources-idUSL2N2O90D0\">Reuters</a>.</p><p>&#34;The big issue for the SEC is to understand if the advisers are conflicted,&#34; one of the sources told <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/usa-sec-spac/refile-exclusive-u-s-sec-focuses-on-bank-fee-conflicts-as-it-steps-up-spac-inquiry-sources-idUSL2N2O90D0\">Reuters</a>.</p><p>The SEC, according to sources, has requested information from top SPAC underwriters including Citigroup, Credit Suisse, Morgan Stanley, and Goldman Sachs. Requests do not imply malpractice.</p><p>SPACs are shell companies that list with the aim of merging with private companies and taking them public.</p><p>This <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/spac-ipo-bill-ackman-reid-hoffman-dave-dewalt-fireeye-2021-3\">method</a> is typically done in lieu of an IPO or a direct listing and has garnered support from Wall Street heavyweights as well as pop icons and professional athletes.</p><p>Management teams of SPACs, also known as sponsors, generally pay banks a 5.5% fee for underwriting the process. Banks, however, can earn more if they also represent the merger target.</p><p>Such conflict of interest could harm investors, sources told <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/usa-sec-spac/refile-exclusive-u-s-sec-focuses-on-bank-fee-conflicts-as-it-steps-up-spac-inquiry-sources-idUSL2N2O90D0\">Reuters</a>.</p><p>Under the current law, banks are not required to disclose their fees in regulatory filings while law and accounting firms are. </p><p>SPACs have exploded in popularity in the last year. In 2020, a total of 248 SPACs raised $83.3 billion according to <a href=\"https://www.spacanalytics.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-id=\"66\" data-m=\"{\">SPAC Analytics</a>. But over halfway through 2021 alone, data already show 368 SPACs that have raised $190 billion, comprising 59% of initial public offerings.</p><p> </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original the start of the pandemic. This is especially the case for beef and veal as well as pork.\n<p class=\"copyright\">iStock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Food prices are on the rise, particularly for beef, per new data from the Labor Department.</li>\n<li>Increases could further strain family budgets, but experts say it won&#39;t last forever.</li>\n<li>Economists project supply chain disruptions will ease in the fall and inflation will go down in 2022.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Prices are on the upswing for many goods, and people could start feeling the pinch at their next grocery store visit. In particular, beef saw a large increase in prices over one month compared to some other food items.</p><p>The price of beef rose by 4.5% in June compared to May, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/consumer-price-index-inflation-june-2021-7\">per new data</a> from the Bureau of Labor Statistics (BLS) released on Tuesday. That was largely in tandem with increases for the cost of eggs (3.1%), pork (3.1%), and ham (3.1%). Compared to a year ago, however, the price of beef was down by 2.8%.</p><p>Other food prices also rose but not to a similar extent. In June, the price of milk rose by 0.5% and potatoes increased by 1.5% compared to May. It will likely increase grocery store costs for many shoppers.</p><p>Prices for various food items have gone up since the start of the pandemic, as seen in the following chart. This is especially the case for beef and veal as well as pork.</p><div class=\"insider-raw-embed\"><iframe title=\"Food price changes since February 2020\" aria-label=\"Interactive line chart\" id=\"datawrapper-chart-uQLB0\" src=\"https://datawrapper.dwcdn.net/uQLB0/1/\" scrolling=\"no\" frameborder=\"0\" style=\"width: 0; min-width: 100% ; border: none;\" height=\"450\"></iframe><script type=\"text/javascript\">!function(){&#34;use strict&#34;;window.addEventListener(&#34;message&#34;,(function(e){if(void 0!==e.data[&#34;datawrapper-height&#34;]){var t=document.querySelectorAll(&#34;iframe&#34;);for(var a in e.data[&#34;datawrapper-height&#34;])for(var r=0;r&#60;t.length;r++){if(t[r].contentWindow===e.source)t[r].style.height=e.data[&#34;datawrapper-height&#34;][a]+&#34;px&#34;}}}))}();</script></div><p>Compared to February 2020, the price of beef and veal was 13.2% higher than the price before the pandemic as of June 2021. The price of pork in June was 11.4% higher than pre-pandemic prices. The prices of some bakery items, such as bread and cakes, have also increased compared to pre-pandemic, but not as high as the increases seen with meat.</p><p>In addition, the cost of food away from home (such as food ordered at restuarants) rose by 0.7% last month, <a href=\"https://www.bls.gov/news.release/cpi.t02.htm\">according to BLS.</a> A note from JP Morgan suggested that could be the result of <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/labor-market-outlook-wage-growth-leisure-hospitality-quits-economic-data-2021-6\">wage increases for hospitality workers</a>, which is getting passed on to menu prices. Additionally, the cost of food away from home is 4.2% higher than a year earlier.</p><p>The rise in food prices aligns with a broader increase in the price of goods throughout the economy. Increased consumer demand <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/why-are-food-prices-rising-grocery-restaurants-inflation-more-expensive-2021-6\">has collided</a> with broken supply chains, causing prices to soar due to shipping delays and other problems that are passed onto consumers.</p><p>Rising food prices are starting to strain family budgets, <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/business/2021/06/28/hunger-philadelphia-free-fridges/\">The Washington Post reported</a>. It may spur additional food insecurity, which had sharply dropped with the passage of President Joe Biden&#39;s stimulus law in March. Some 20 million US adults reported not getting enough to eat at least sometimes in mid-June, per <a href=\"https://www.cbpp.org/research/poverty-and-inequality/tracking-the-covid-19-recessions-effects-on-food-housing-and\">the left-leaning Center on Budget and Policy Priorities.</a></p><p>So far, experts say there&#39;s little sign that prices will spiral out of control. Economists at the nonpartisan Congressional Budget Office and the Federal Reserve project inflation will fall to more manageable levels of 2% across the economy as soon as next year.</p><p>Ian Shepherdson, chief economist for Pantheon Macroeconomics argued price increases will prove to be &#34;transient,&#34; or short-lived as the economy reopens and broken supply chains start mending themselves. </p><p>&#34;Inflation expectations have risen merely in line with the increase in food and energy inflation, as usual, with no sign that core expectations are being elevated,&#34; Ian href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>If you&#39;re in the market for a used car or truck, get ready to pay a lot.</p><p>The Bureau of Labor Statistics&#39; <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/consumer-price-index-inflation-june-2021-7\">monthly Consumer Price Index release</a> showed that inflation in June was much higher than economists had expected. One of the biggest contributors to overall prices rising was the 10.5% increase in used car and truck prices between May and June.</p><p>Looking at changes over the last year, used cars in June 2021 were 45.2% more expensive than in June 2020.</p><p>New cars also got more expensive, with prices increasing 2.0% between May and June, but those prices have been going up much more slowly than for used cars.</p><p>The whopping jump in used car prices was the biggest monthly increase since the Bureau of Labor Statistics started tracking these figures in 1953. It follows two other historically high monthly increases of 7.3% in May and 10.0% in April.</p><div class=\"insider-raw-embed\"><iframe title=\"Price changes for new and used cars\" aria-label=\"Interactive line chart\" id=\"datawrapper-chart-dkhpo\" src=\"https://datawrapper.dwcdn.net/dkhpo/1/\" scrolling=\"no\" frameborder=\"0\" style=\"width: 0; min-width: 100% ; border: none;\" height=\"450\"></iframe><script type=\"text/javascript\">!function(){&#34;use strict&#34;;window.addEventListener(&#34;message&#34;,(function(e){if(void 0!==e.data[&#34;datawrapper-height&#34;]){var t=document.querySelectorAll(&#34;iframe&#34;);for(var a in e.data[&#34;datawrapper-height&#34;])for(var r=0;r&#60;t.length;r++){if(t[r].contentWindow===e.source)t[r].style.height=e.data[&#34;datawrapper-height&#34;][a]+&#34;px&#34;}}}))}();</script></div><p>The used car market has gotten so upended that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/used-cars-more-expensive-than-new-auto-industry-chip-shortage-2021-7\">several models are now cheaper to buy new than used</a>.</p><p>There are several reasons for the massive jumps in used car prices over the last few months. A <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/global-chip-shortage-could-last-another-2-years-experts-say-2021-5\">global semiconductor shortage</a> has left automakers without the computer chips needed to make new cars, cutting off supplies of new cars.</p><p>Rental companies <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/buying-a-used-rental-car-as-hertz-rental-companies-go-bankrupt-2020-5\">sold off large swathes of their fleets last summer</a> amid collapsing demand during the pandemic. Now that demand has come back, those companies are stocking back up, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/rental-car-used-auctions-rental-shortage-hertz-enterprise-chip-shortage-2021-5\">including turning to the used car market themselves</a> and competing with regular consumers.</p><p>Despite the huge price increases of the last few months, relief could be on its way. Insider&#39;s Tim Levin noted that according to Cox Automotive, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/why-are-used-cars-so-expensive-now-shortages-pandemic-rentals-2021-7\">wholesale car prices declined between May and June</a>, and retail prices could follow.</p><p>Similarly, <a href=\"https://www.npr.org/2021/07/13/1014697915/inflation-is-still-high-used-car-prices-could-help-explain-what-happens-next?utm_medium=social&utm_term=nprnews&utm_campaign=npr&utm_source=twitter.com=twitter.com\">NPR&#39;s Scott Horsely</a> reported that &#34;prices dealers pay for used cars at massive auctions across the country finally dipped in June.&#34;</p><p>A research note from Morgan Stanley also predicted that as the auto market gradually returns to normal, &#34;looking ahead we should see used car price increases begin to the decelerate as more recent industry data has started to turn modestly lower.&#34;</p><p>But for now, used cars are still quite expensive.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Monday, calling the attorney a &#34;bad human.&#34;</p><p>The Tesla CEO was defending his company&#39;s 2016 <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-court-tesla-solarcity-acquisition-energy-damages-2021-7\">acquisition of SolarCity</a>, a solar-panel company <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-tesla-solarcity-merger-frenzied-plan-new-filings-show-2019-10\">founded by his cousins</a>. The plaintiffs claim that the deal amounted to a bailout of SolarCity.</p><p>Musk gave lengthy responses to yes-or-no questions during the trial at Delaware&#39;s Court of Chancery, frustrating the plaintiffs&#39; lawyer, Randall Baron, who told Musk he was holding up the trial, <a href=\"https://www.delawareonline.com/story/news/2021/07/12/elon-musk-defends-solarcity-purchase-trial-held-delaware-court/7935054002/\">the Delaware News Journal</a> and <a href=\"https://apnews.com/article/business-09dfd1c03b59b1af55aa967d1c093482\">The Associated Press</a> reported.</p><p>Musk told Baron that some of his questions were &#34;really tricky and deceptive,&#34; the reports said.</p><p>&#34;I think you are a bad human being,&#34; Musk told Baron after the lawyer asked him if he was being &#34;derisive&#34; in his answers to questions, the Journal and <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/technology/2021/07/12/elon-musk-trial-tesla/\">The Washington Post reported</a>.</p><p>&#34;You were mentored by criminals, then continued to be mentored by criminals,&#34; Musk told Baron, citing examples of <a href=\"https://www.latimes.com/business/la-fi-lerach12feb12-story.html\">criminal wrongdoing by a former partner</a> at a firm that was a predecessor of Baron&#39;s law firm, Robbins Geller Rudman &#38; Dowd LLP, The Post reported.</p><p>Tesla shareholders <a href=\"http://climatecasechart.com/climate-change-litigation/wp-content/uploads/sites/16/case-documents/2017/20170316_docket-12711-VCS_complaint.pdf\">filed the lawsuit in 2017</a>, accusing Musk of pressuring the company&#39;s board to effectively bail out SolarCity in <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/elon-musk-made-6-billion-error-buying-solarcity-tesla-stock-2020-2\">the $2.6 billion deal</a>. Musk owned a roughly 22% stake in Tesla and SolarCity at the time, <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/us-tesla-solarcity-trial-idTRNIKBN2EI0UO\">according to Reuters</a>.</p><p>Lyndon Rive, SolarCity&#39;s cofounder and Musk&#39;s cousin, described the firm as &#34;super low on cash&#34; and in need of capital <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-tesla-solarcity-merger-frenzied-plan-new-filings-show-2019-10\">in an email to an unnamed person</a> in 2016, soon after the deal was announced.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/new-austin-homes-neighborhood-tesla-brookfield-real-estate-development-2021-7?r=US&IR=TIR=T\" data-e2e-name=\"inline-read-more-link\">Tesla and real-estate giant Brookfield are building a neighborhood in Austin full of renewable-energy tech</a></em></p><p>Musk denied that he had benefited from the deal. &#34;Since it was a stock-for-stock transaction and I owned almost exactly the same percentage of both there was no financial gain,&#34; he told the court on Monday, <a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2021/07/12/elon-musk-testifies-in-tesla-shareholder-lawsuit-over-solarcity-acquisition.html\">according to CNBC</a>.</p><p>In an email to Insider, Baron said that the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-court-tesla-solarcity-acquisition-energy-damages-2021-7\">full damages sought</a> in the lawsuit were between $2.2 billion and $2.6 billion, though Musk could pay less if he&#39;s found liable.</p><p>SolarCity became Tesla Energy, Tesla&#39;s solar-power division, after the acquisition. Greg Abbott promised that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/texas-democrats-walking-out-leaving-state-to-block-gop-bills-2021-7\">Democratic lawmakers who staged a walkout in Texas</a> would be arrested.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OF4X6tmmcDk\">Speaking to KVUE on Monday</a>, the two-term Republican criticized Democratic lawmakers who fled en masse to block several conservative bills from passing in a legislative special session.</p><p>&#34;As soon as they come back in the state of Texas, they will be arrested, they will be cabined inside the Texas Capitol until they get their job done,&#34; he said.</p><p>Democratic leaders in the Texas House <a href=\"https://twitter.com/cassi_pollock/status/1414662554140426248\">said on Monday</a> that they had flown to Washington, DC, to &#34;refuse to let the Republican-led legislature force through dangerous legislation that would trample on Texans&#39; freedom to vote.&#34;</p><p>Under Texas law, two-thirds of lawmakers must be present for legislative business to proceed.</p><p>Abbott <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/texas-gov-abbott-special-legislative-session-agenda-right-wing-causes-2021-7\">convened the special session</a> earlier this month to pass a litany of conservative priorities, including legislation targeting voting, abortion access, transgender rights, and critical race theory.</p><p>The marquee issue is a restrictive voting bill that Republican lawmakers have sought largely in response to President Donald Trump&#39;s loss to Joe Biden.</p><p>The bill would modify early-voting hours, curb the 24/7 voting centers <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/24/us/politics/texas-republicans-voting.html\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"75343e11df986a07f3b7412c32c84530\">that were popular with shift workers</a> in Democratic-leaning Harris County in last year&#39;s presidential election, and scrap straight-ticket voting, among other measures.</p><p>Democratic state senators on Friday introduced a bill called the Barbara Jordan Fair Elections Act, named after the revered Black senator, designed to <a href=\"https://www.dallasnews.com/news/politics/2021/07/09/democratic-senators-decry-texas-gops-election-bills-push-back-with-one-named-for-barbara-jordan/\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"66f4d310fc28db59ae5c7586e0f328fa\">expand access to voting</a>, allowing for online and same-day voter registration, among other measures, <a href=\"https://www.dallasnews.com/news/politics/2021/07/09/democratic-senators-decry-texas-gops-election-bills-push-back-with-one-named-for-barbara-jordan/\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"66f4d310fc28db59ae5c7586e0f328fa\">according to The Dallas Morning News</a>.</p><p>However, the GOP-dominated Legislature is unlikely to take up that bill.</p><p>While no Democratic state senators had accompanied their House counterparts to the nation&#39;s capital as of Tuesday, a Democratic official said several senators might travel there, <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/07/12/us/politics/texas-democrats-voting-bill.html\">according to The New York Times</a>.</p><p>Abbott told KVUE that he would not relent from carrying out his legislative objectives.</p><p>The governor said he would &#34;continue to call special session after special session&#34; until Democratic lawmakers are present.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read and the grill maker could secure a billion-dollar valuation","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/warren-buffett-banker-byron-trott-bdt-weber-grills-ipo-filing-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3e789b42f43f001ddfdf92?format=jpeg\" alt=\"warren buffett\" height=\"1728\" width=\"3456\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Warren Buffett.\n<p class=\"copyright\">AP Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Warren Buffett&#39;s longtime banker plans to take Weber public, SEC filings show.</li>\n<li>Byron Trott&#39;s BDT has been the grilling company&#39;s majority shareholder since 2010.</li>\n<li>Buffett has lauded Trott&#39;s dealmaking skills, expertise, and trustworthiness.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Warren Buffett&#39;s favorite banker has filed to take Weber public, paving the way for the grilling specialist to deliver a billion-dollar IPO.</p><p>BDT Capital Partners, helmed by founder and CEO Byron Trott, has been Weber&#39;s majority shareholder since 2010 and has agreed to sponsor its IPO. Weber boasts a global installed base of 50 million grills, and commands a 24% share of the global market, <a href=\"https://sec.report/Document/0001193125-21-212480/\">according to its draft IPO filing</a>.</p><p>Notably, Weber has enjoyed some benefits from the COVID-19 pandemic, including higher demand for outdoor spaces and activities thanks to social-distancing measures and lockdowns. The company&#39;s revenue surged 62% year-on-year to $963 million in the six months to March 31, and its net income tripled to about $74 million during that period.</p><p>Weber raked in over $1.5 billion of revenue in the year to September 30, up from $1.3 billion in its previous fiscal year, making a billion-dollar public valuation for the company seem reasonable.</p><p>Trott, who worked at Goldman Sachs before launching BDT in 2009, has advised Buffett on several Berkshire Hathaway deals. Those include the conglomerate&#39;s purchases of McLane, Marmon, and Pilot Flying J over the past two decades, as well as its financing of <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/warren-buffett-spent-billions-help-mars-buy-wrigley-2008-crisis-2020-7\">Mars&#39; acquisition of Wrigley</a> in 2008.</p><p>&#34;He understands Berkshire far better than any investment banker with whom we have talked and - it hurts me to say this - earns his fee,&#34; Buffett, a notorious skeptic of bankers, said about Trott in his <a href=\"https://www.berkshirehathaway.com/2003ar/2003ar.pdf\">2003 letter to shareholders</a>.</p><p>&#34;Byron is the rare investment banker who puts himself in his client&#39;s shoes,&#34; the investor and Berkshire CEO said in his <a href=\"https://www.berkshirehathaway.com/letters/2007ltr.pdf\">2007 letter</a>. &#34;Charlie and I trust him completely.&#34;</p><p>Trott&#39;s BDT has raised over $18 billion in total across its investment funds, and made more than $7 billion of co-investments, according to Weber&#39;s IPO filing. Its non-Berkshire deals include JAB&#39;s past purchases of Panera Bread and Krispy Kreme, and JAB-owned Keurig&#39;s takeover of Dr Pepper Snapple a few years ago.</p><div
