(small)</bi-shortcode><p>While it may be the middle of summer, for me it&#39;s always soup season. Anyone who has ever been blessed enough to eat with me at a restaurant knows that I&#39;m always going to ask the server the same question: &#34;What&#39;s your soup of the day?&#34; </p><p>Soup is one of those comfort foods that I&#39;m always in the mood for - I&#39;ve been known to get an early morning cup of chicken lemon rice soup alongside my omelet at a diner. However, because I didn&#39;t have the proper equipment, I always categorized most of my favorite soups as a &#34;restaurant food,&#34; or recipes that seemed either too complicated, difficult, or ambitious for me to make at home. </p><bi-shortcode id=\"related-article-module\" class=\"mceNonEditable\" data-type=\"5909e3f0fcd8eb1f008b4884\" data-title=\"The best immersion blenders\" data-url=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/best-immersion-blender\" data-thumbnail=\"https://i.insider.com/5f4fb3ec7ed0ee001e25cfcf\" data-shortcode-display-text=\"Related Article Module: The best immersion blenders\"> </bi-shortcode><p>That was until I tested the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.williams-sonoma.com%2Fproducts%2Fbreville-control-grip-immersion-blender%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Breville Control Grip Immersion Blender</a>. For $100, this has everything I need to make my favorite soups, dips, salsas, and more at home. Even though I&#39;m relegated to the role of my girlfriend&#39;s sous chef in our apartment, home cooks will love the simplicity, versatility, and easy clean up that comes with the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.williams-sonoma.com%2Fproducts%2Fbreville-control-grip-immersion-blender%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Breville Control Grip Immersion Blender</a>. </p><h2>What you get</h2><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.williams-sonoma.com%2Fproducts%2Fbreville-control-grip-immersion-blender%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5df7d9e4fd9db264124e3363?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Breville Control Grip set\" height=\"900\" width=\"1200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The set comes with a motorized handle, immersion blender, jug, chopping bowl, and whisk.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Amazon</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p><p>It comes with five major components - a motorized handle, immersion blender, whisk, chopping bowl, and extra-large jug.</p><p>The motorized handle can be used with the immersion blender, whisk, and chopping bowl, just click it into place and it automatically connects with whichever tool you&#39;re using. The motor gets up to 280 watts but can be adjusted within 15 different speed settings depending on how chunky you want your final product to turn out. While Breville makes more powerful blenders than this, I&#39;ve never had any issues blending cooked potatoes and cauliflower into a creamy soup. </p><p>The immersion blender is 8-inches long, allowing you to fully submerge the blades into deep pots and its bell-shape design helps increase blending ability without splashing all over your kitchen counters. The bottom of the blender has a non-scratch exterior so you don&#39;t have to worry about ruining your pots if you get too close to the bottom or sides of your cookware.</p><p>The whisk attachment is just as easy to use and clean. Click it into the motor and you&#39;re ready to mix, aerate, and whisk anything you need. </p><p>While it&#39;s not technically a food processor, the chopping bowl has stainless steel blades that will perform the same essential function. Click the motor into the lid of the chopping bowl, and it automatically connects to the blades at the bottom. Plus, each part of the chopping bowl easily separates when it&#39;s time for cleanup. </p><p>You can use the large jug to stabilize the chopping bowl or to hold all the ingredients as you blend or whisk with the attachments.</p><h2>How the Breville Control Grip Immersion Blender performed</h2><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.williams-sonoma.com%2Fproducts%2Fbreville-control-grip-immersion-blender%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5df7dad2fd9db20484463ac8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Immersion Blender motor\" height=\"900\" width=\"1200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>We were able to blend a corn tortilla soup (left) and potato leek soup (right) in less than 10 minutes.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Danny Bakst/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p><p>The <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.williams-sonoma.com%2Fproducts%2Fbreville-control-grip-immersion-blender%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Breville Control Grip</a> couldn&#39;t be easier to handle during testing.</p><p>The motor/handle is ergonomically designed for a natural grip and the material is soft to the touch. The button to turn on the motor is right where you&#39;d expect it to be when gripping the device, and you can easily adjust the speed with the top dial while you&#39;re still blending. This is important because you&#39;re not supposed to start the blender at high speeds right away but instead are supposed to slowly build up to higher speeds.</p><p>So far, we&#39;ve cooked several different soups with the blender attachment, including cauliflower and onion, roasted tomato and garlic, potato leek, and tortilla. </p><p>While blending time differs depending on how chunky you want your final dish, it never took us more than 10 minutes to complete the blending step of any recipe.</p><p>The scratch guard on the blender allowed it to glide along the bottom of our large pot without fear of ruining the surface of our cookware, and it was easily washed with hot water and soap. Additionally, we never had any issues with food getting jammed in the blender or the motor overheating.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.williams-sonoma.com%2Fproducts%2Fbreville-control-grip-immersion-blender%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5df7dc89fd9db242c77d102a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"soups\" height=\"900\" width=\"1200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>After both soups were blended to our desired level of chunkiness, we topped the potato leek soup with turkey bacon and chopped green onion, and the tortilla soup with chickpeas and diced avocado.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Danny Bakst/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p><p>Like the blender, using the chopping bowl is also intuitive.</p><p>So far, we&#39;ve made a white bean hummus dip and a parsley-based pesto. The pesto blended relatively quickly, but the beans took a little bit longer to blend down to our desired creaminess compared to the soups we&#39;d made with the immersion blender. That said, it&#39;s not like holding the button down a little longer is very taxing so this wasn&#39;t too much of an issue.</p><p>For denser items like chickpeas, the blades didn&#39;t seem powerful enough to keep grinding at times, so we had to transfer everything to the extra-large jug and use the immersion blender instead.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.williams-sonoma.com%2Fproducts%2Fbreville-control-grip-immersion-blender%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5df7df49fd9db208b87d1792?format=jpeg\" alt=\"White Bean Hummus dip\" height=\"900\" width=\"1200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The chopping bowl is really easy to use, just put in all your ingredients and attach the motor to the top.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Danny Bakst/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p><p>If you&#39;re pressed for time, you can always increase the speed of the motor, but again, gradually increase the power of the motor until you get to the speed you want. </p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.williams-sonoma.com%2Fproducts%2Fbreville-control-grip-immersion-blender%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5df7df5dfd9db245752e32e7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Chopping bowl final results\" height=\"900\" width=\"1200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Our parsley pesto (left) and white bean and rosemary dip (right) blended with the press of a button.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Danny Bakst/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p><p>We haven&#39;t felt the need to use the jug as a stabilizer for the chopping bowl and have just placed the chopping bowl directly on the counter. In fact, we haven&#39;t used the jug much because we use the immersion blender mostly in our pots.</p><p>We don&#39;t eat eggs or whipped cream in my apartment, so we haven&#39;t had a reason to use the whisking tool yet either. There&#39;s nothing really special to this attachment but I can see it being useful for things like pancakes, waffles, and even desserts.</p><h2>The bottom line</h2><p>The <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.williams-sonoma.com%2Fproducts%2Fbreville-control-grip-immersion-blender%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Breville Control Grip Immersion Blender</a> has become our favorite tool in the kitchen because I no longer have to go out to try all my favorite soups. With all the different attachments included alongside the blender, we now have the ability to make any recipe we come across in our favorite cookbooks. </p><p>There are plenty of immersion blenders out there that will get the job done, but the reason why this one is the top pick in <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/best-immersion-blender\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">our buying guide</a> is because of its versatility and value. For $100, you get a powerful motor and useful attachments that can help make a variety of dishes. It&#39;s an easily justifiable purchase for any person who likes to cook and is looking for ways to make their favorite restaurant dishes at home. </p><bi-shortcode id=\"commerce-link\" (Danny Bakst)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5df7e0f1fd9db26b6f513b42?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn27@2020_1/2021/07/13/17-22-11-122_14564258f7aa34aa.webp","https://i.insider.com/5df7d9e4fd9db264124e3363?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn56@2020_5/2021/07/13/17-22-22-749_e4be786fdf8bf556.webp","https://i.insider.com/5df7dad2fd9db20484463ac8?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn100@2020_5/2021/07/13/17-22-23-477_b1c4e68f7bb5a8e1.webp","https://i.insider.com/5df7dc89fd9db242c77d102a?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn59@2020_5/2021/07/13/17-22-22-152_f2e795e85f30b505.webp","https://i.insider.com/5df7df49fd9db208b87d1792?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn7@2020_6/2021/07/13/17-22-22-592_5d742b88080c1eef.webp","https://i.insider.com/5df7df5dfd9db245752e32e7?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn96@2020_1/2021/07/13/17-22-23-656_44a378cee1771599.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn12@2020_2/2021/07/13/17-22-25-174_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=lQmtclAnG8c:9zSg_232wlw:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn35@2020_2/2021/07/13/17-22-26-062_6927c5f6b49e2a57.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=lQmtclAnG8c:9zSg_232wlw:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn39@2020_5/2021/07/13/17-22-22-489_b22e68b4f506fc31.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn83@2020_2/2021/07/13/17-22-23-761_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=lQmtclAnG8c:9zSg_232wlw:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn12@2020_6/2021/07/13/17-22-22-289_2cd80d16746cc259.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/lQmtclAnG8c":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn39@2020_5/2021/07/13/17-22-26-075_7454170cfc251331.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626196914896},{"createdTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:54","updatedTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:54","title":"How a cheap Swedish submarine 'ran rings' around a US aircraft carrier and its sub-hunting escorts","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-swedish-sub-ran-rings-around-us-aircraft-carrier-escorts-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5c41e98edde8671fb2327622?format=jpeg\" alt=\"USS Ronald Reagan\" height=\"2500\" width=\"5000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>USS Ronald Reagan.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mass Communication Specialist 2nd Class Kaila V. Peters/U.S. Navy via AP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>In 2005, the US Navy&#39;s new aircraft carrier, USS Ronald Reagan, sank after being hit by torpedoes.</li>\n<li>This didn&#39;t happen in combat but during a war game pitting a carrier task force, and its anti-submarine escorts, against a Swedish sub.</li>\n<li>That sub, HSMS Gotland, pulled off that feat despite being a relatively cheap diesel-powered boat.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>In 2005, <a href=\"https://www.19fortyfive.com/2021/04/uss-ronald-reagan-the-aircraft-carrier-that-could-start-a-war/\">USS Ronald Reagan</a>, a newly constructed $6.2 billion aircraft carrier, sank after being hit by multiple torpedoes.</p><p>Fortunately, this did not occur in actual combat, but was simulated as part of a war game pitting a carrier task force including numerous antisubmarine escorts against HSMS Gotland, a small Swedish diesel-powered submarine displacing 1,600 tons. Yet despite making multiple attacks runs on the Reagan, the Gotland was never detected.</p><p>This outcome was replicated time and time again over two years of war games, with opposing destroyers and nuclear attack submarines succumbing to the stealthy Swedish sub.</p><p>Naval analyst Norman Polmar said the <a href=\"https://www.19fortyfive.com/2021/01/gotland-swedens-stealth-submarine-that-sunk-a-carrier/\">Gotland</a> &#34;ran rings&#34; around the American carrier task force. Another source claimed US antisubmarine specialists were &#34;demoralized&#34; by the experience.</p><p>How was the Gotland able to evade the Reagan&#39;s elaborate antisubmarine defenses involving multiple ships and aircraft employing a multitude of sensors? And even more importantly, how was a relatively cheap submarine costing around $100 million - roughly the cost of a single F-35 stealth fighter today - able to accomplish that? After all, the US Navy decommissioned its last diesel submarine in 1990.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5442f8bd69bedd835fef1d8c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Swedish submarine Navy\" height=\"1281\" width=\"2659\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Sweden&#39;s HMS Gotland with the USS Ronald Reagan in the background.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"http://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:HMS_Gotland_with_USS_Ronald_Reagan.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">US Navy</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Diesel submarines in the past were limited by the need to operate noisy, air-consuming engines that meant they could remain underwater for only a few days before needing to surface. Naturally, a submarine is most vulnerable, and can be most easily tracked, when surfaced, even when using a snorkel.</p><p>Submarines powered by nuclear reactors, on the other hand, do not require large air supplies to operate, and can run much more quietly for <em>months</em> at a time underwater - and they can swim faster while at it.</p><p>However, the 200-foot-long Swedish Gotland-class submarines, introduced in 1996, were the first to employ an Air Independent Propulsion (AIP) system - in this case, the Stirling engine. A Stirling engine charges the submarine&#39;s 75-kilowatt battery using <em>liquid</em> oxygen.</p><p>With the Stirling, a Gotland-class submarine can remain undersea for up to two weeks sustaining an average speed of 6 mph - or it can expend its battery power to surge up to 23 mph. A conventional diesel engine is used for operation on the surface or while employing the snorkel.</p><p>The Stirling-powered Gotland runs more quietly than even a nuclear-powered sub, which must employ noise-producing coolant pumps in their reactors.</p><p>The Gotland class does <a href=\"https://foxtrotalpha.jalopnik.com/sweden-has-a-sub-thats-so-deadly-the-us-navy-hired-it-t-1649695984\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-cke-saved-href=\"http://foxtrotalpha.jalopnik.com/sweden-has-a-sub-thats-so-deadly-the-us-navy-hired-it-t-1649695984\">possess many other features</a> that make it adept at evading detection.</p><p>It mounts 27 electromagnets designed to counteract its magnetic signature to Magnetic Anomaly Detectors. Its hull benefits from sonar-resistant coatings, while the tower is made of radar-absorbent materials. Machinery on the interior is coated with rubber acoustic-deadening buffers to minimize detectability by sonar.</p><p>The Gotland is also exceedingly maneuverable thanks to the combined six maneuvering surfaces on its X-shaped rudder and sail, allowing it to operate close to the sea floor and pull off tight turns.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60edc15061b8600019f16d28?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Swedish navy submarine HMS Gotland in San Diego\" height=\"1330\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>HMS Gotland in San Diego Harbor during Fleet Week San Diego, October 1, 2005.\n<p class=\"copyright\">US Navy/Mate 2nd Class Patricia R. Totemeier</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Because the stealthy boat proved the ultimate challenge to US antisubmarine ships in international exercises, the US Navy leased the Gotland and its crew for two entire years to conduct antisubmarine exercises. The results convinced the US Navy its undersea sensors simply were not up to dealing with the stealthy AIP boats.</p><p>However, the Gotland was merely the first of many AIP-powered submarine designs - some with twice the underwater endurance. And Sweden is by no means the only country to be fielding them.</p><p>China has two diesel submarine types using Stirling engines. Fifteen of the earlier Type 039A Yuan class have been built in four different variants, with more than 20 more planned or already under construction.</p><p>Beijing also has a single Type 032 Qing-class vessel that can remain underwater for 30 days. It believed to be the largest operational diesel submarine in the world, and boasts seven Vertical Launch System cells capable of firing off cruise missiles and ballistic missiles.</p><p>Russia debuted with the experimental Lada-class Sankt Peterburg, which uses hydrogen fuel cells for power. It is an evolution of its widely produced Kilo-class submarine. However, sea trials found that the cells provided only half of the expected output, and the type was not approved for production.</p><p>However, in 2013 the Russian Navy announced it would produce two heavily redesigned Ladas, the Kronstadt and Velikiye Luki, expected by the end of the decade.</p><p>Other producers of AIP diesel submarines include Spain, France, Japan and Germany. These countries have in turn sold them to navies across the world, including to India, Israel, Pakistan and South Korea.</p><p>Submarines using AIP systems have evolved into larger, more heavily armed and more expensive types, including the German Dolphin-class and the French Scorpene-class submarines.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60b859b6bee0fc0019d5b04f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Indian Navy Scorpene-class submarine Karanj\" height=\"1287\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The Indian Navy&#39;s third Scorpene-class submarine, Karanj, at its launch in Mumbai, January 31, 2018.\n<p class=\"copyright\">PUNIT PARANJPE/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The US Navy has no intention to field diesel submarines again, however, preferring to stick to nuclear submarines that cost multiple billions of dollars. It&#39;s tempting to see that as the Pentagon choosing once again a more expensive weapon system over a vastly more cost-efficient alternative. It&#39;s not <em>quite </em>that simple, however.</p><p>Diesel submarines are ideal for patrolling close to friendly shores. But US subs off Asia and Europe need to travel <em>thousands </em>of miles just to get there, and then remain deployed for months at a time. A diesel submarine may be able to traverse that distance - but it would then require frequent refueling at sea to complete a long deployment.</p><p>Remember the Gotland? It was shipped back to Sweden on a mobile dry dock rather than making the journey on its own power.</p><p>Though the new AIP-equipped diesel subs may be able to go weeks without surfacing, that&#39;s still not as good as going <em>months</em> without having to do so. And furthermore, a diesel submarine - with or without AIP - can&#39;t sustain high underwater speeds for very long, unlike a nuclear submarine.</p><p>A diesel sub will be most effective when ambushing a hostile fleet <a href=\"https://warisboring.com/chinese-subs-finally-get-a-shot-at-american-carriers-ac3fc030890a#.wqq3vuc11\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-cke-saved-href=\"https://warisboring.com/chinese-subs-finally-get-a-shot-at-american-carriers-ac3fc030890a#.wqq3vuc11\">whose position has already been &#34;cued&#34; by friendly intelligence assets</a>. However, the slow, sustainable underwater speed of AIP-powered diesel submarines make them less than ideal for stalking prey over vast expanses of water.</p><p>These limitations don&#39;t pose a problem to diesel subs operating relatively close to friendly bases, defending littoral waters. But while diesel submarines may be great while operating close to home - the US Navy usually doesn&#39;t.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6078949574da0300181e1f1a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Navy submarine\" height=\"1333\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>US Navy fast-attack submarine USS Asheville and US 7th Fleet flagship USS Blue Ridge in the Philippine Sea.\n<p class=\"copyright\">US Navy/MC2 Adam K. Thomas</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Still, the fact that one could build or acquire three or four diesel submarines costing $500 to $800 million each for the price of a single nuclear submarine gives them undeniable appeal.</p><p>Proponents argue that the United States could forward deploy diesel subs to bases in allied nations, without facing the political constraints posed by nuclear submarines. Furthermore, advanced diesel submarines might serve as a good counter to an adversary&#39;s stealthy sub fleet.</p><p>However, the US Navy is more interested in pursuing the development of unmanned drone submarines. Meanwhile, China is working on long-enduring AIP systems using lithium-ion batteries, and France is developing a new <a href=\"https://foxtrotalpha.jalopnik.com/is-this-jumbo-diesel-electric-submarine-a-true-nuclear-1652659060\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-cke-saved-href=\"http://foxtrotalpha.jalopnik.com/is-this-jumbo-diesel-electric-submarine-a-true-nuclear-1652659060\">large AIP-equipped diesel submarine</a> version of its Barracuda-class nuclear attack submarine.</p><p>The advent of cheap, stealthy and long-enduring diesel submarines is yet another factor placing carriers and other expensive surface warships at greater risk when operating close to defended coastlines.</p><p>Diesel submarines benefitting from AIP will serve as a deadly and cost-effective means of defending littoral waters, though whether they will can carve out a role for themselves in blue-water naval forces operating far from home is less clear.</p><p><em>Sébastien Roblin writes on the technical, historical and political aspects of international security and conflict for publications including the <a href=\"https://nationalinterest.org/profile/sebastien-roblin\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-auth=\"NotApplicable\" data-cke-saved-href=\"https://nationalinterest.org/profile/sebastien-roblin\">The National Interest</a>, <a href=\"https://www.nbcnews.com/think/opinion/navy-spent-30b-16-years-fight-iran-littoral-combat-ship-ncna1031806\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-auth=\"NotApplicable\" data-cke-saved-href=\"https://www.nbcnews.com/think/opinion/navy-spent-30b-16-years-fight-iran-littoral-combat-ship-ncna1031806\">NBC News</a>, <a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/sites/sebastienroblin/#457ee8ba2082\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-auth=\"NotApplicable\" noreferrer\" data-auth=\"NotApplicable\" data-cke-saved-href=\"https://warisboring.com/author/sebastien-a-roblin/\">War is Boring</a>. With the <a href=\"https://www.anrdoezrs.net/links/6415797/type/dlg/https://www.kitchenaid.com/countertop-appliances/stand-mixers/attachments/p.3-piece-pasta-roller-and-cutter-set.ksmpra.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow sponsored\">KitchenAid 3-Piece Pasta Roller &#38; Cutter Attachment Set</a>, you turn your KitchenAid stand mixer into a one-stop pasta shop. This set comes with a pasta roller that rolls six-inch sheets of pasta to eight different thicknesses, a fettuccine cutter, a spaghetti cutter, and a cleaning brush. All of the pieces are made in Italy.</p><p>How does it work? First, you prepare the dough using the mixer, then you flatten the dough and feed it into the rollers on the 2-speed setting.&#160;This will knead it. You repeat the rolling process until the dough is smooth and pliable. You slowly decrease the thickness of the dough until it is at your desired thickness. Then, to make the noodles, you either feed it through the spaghetti cutter or the fettuccine cutter.</p><p>It took me some practice to get the dough just right to feed it through the rollers, but once I got the hang of it, it was easy and fun. I'm impressed with how durable the pieces are. Do not put coffee or peanuts in this attachment because it could damage the grinding mechanism. Before you use the attachment, clean it with a mild detergent to remove any oils used to protect the device from rust. Also, the mill is not dishwasher safe so use the brush that comes with the kit to clean it off or wash by hand if you need to.</p><p>The mill can produce cracked to extra fine consistencies. The mill features symbols for the finest grind and the coarsest grind, and there are several notches in between. First, you choose a setting, put the grain in the hopper, and start the mixer at speed 10. If the grind is not precisely to your liking, adjust the knob until you get it as coarse or fine as you want. If the mixer appears to be overheating, turn it off for at least 45 minutes before continuing.</p><p>Those who enjoy multigrain bread and cracking grains for porridge will like that this accessory can mill very coarsely. However, be wary of milling massive amounts of grain on the finest setting at high speeds.</p><p>Be aware that the mill seems to work best with newer models in the Professional and Artisan series and is geared toward the home baking enthusiast who needs about two or three pounds of flour per week.</p>\n\tThe best KitchenAid attachment for food processing\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60ec870b61b8600019f16a8e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"best kitchenaid attachments 2021 commercial food processor\" height=\"732\" width=\"976\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.anrdoezrs.net/links/6415797/type/dlg/https://www.kitchenaid.com/countertop-appliances/stand-mixers/attachments/p.food-processor-with-commercial-style-dicing-kit.ksm2fpa.html\" target=\"_blank\">Amazon</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<h3>Drastically decrease the time it takes to prep ingredients for your meals by using the <a href=\"https://www.anrdoezrs.net/links/6415797/type/dlg/https://www.kitchenaid.com/countertop-appliances/stand-mixers/attachments/p.food-processor-with-commercial-style-dicing-kit.ksm2fpa.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">KitchenAid Commerical Food Processor Attachment</a> to slice, shred, and julienne vegetables, cheeses, and fruits.</h3><p><strong>Pros: </strong>Streamlined design is easy to clean, durable</p><p><strong>Cons: </strong>Unlike your standard food processor, it does not mix food together</p><p>The <a href=\"https://www.anrdoezrs.net/links/6415797/type/dlg/https://www.kitchenaid.com/countertop-appliances/stand-mixers/attachments/p.food-processor-with-commercial-style-dicing-kit.ksm2fpa.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">KitchenAid Commercial Food Processor Attachment</a> (model KSM2FPA) comes with shredding, julienning, and slicing discs. It is made out of plastic with metal blades and comes with a one-year replacement warranty.</p><p>This attachment does everything a top-quality food processor does, without the need for a new appliance that takes up extra space in your kitchen.</p><p>This Commercial Food Processor Attachment is the pricier sibling of the similar <a href=\"https://www.anrdoezrs.net/links/6415797/type/dlg/https://www.kitchenaid.com/countertop-appliances/stand-mixers/attachments/p.food-processor-slice-and-shredder.ksm1fpa.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">KSM1FPA</a>. The main differences between the two is the higher-end KSM2FPA comes with a storage case, commercial-style dicing kit, and currently costs a bit more. I no longer buy ground meat. I do it all myself, and the results are always far superior to what you would buy pre-packaged at the store. I keep my grinder in the freezer so it's always ready to go when I want ground meat. It's important to chill the grinder to protect against temperature increases that could lead to bacteria growth while grinding.</p><p>One of my favorite creations was half pork jowl bacon/half beef burgers. href=\"https://www.gettyimages.com/detail/news-photo/trump-supporters-near-the-us-capitol-following-a-quot-stop-news-photo/1230476001?adppopup=true\" target=\"_blank\">NurPhoto/Getty</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>A federal judge agreed to free a QAnon believer charged in the January 6 riot at the US Capitol.</li>\n<li>The judge decided the man couldn&#39;t have planned the attack because &#34;he had no basic understanding of where he even was that day.&#34;</li>\n<li>In a January 6 video, the man claims he was at the White House when he was on Capitol grounds.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>A federal judge agreed on Tuesday to free an Iowa man from jail more than six months after his videotaped confrontation of a police officer inside the U.S. Capitol became one of the most menacing images of the Jan. 6 riots.</p><p><a href=\"https://apnews.com/article/donald-trump-capitol-siege-b6587af22fb1ef19b9cd7a7e21f51e16\">Douglas Jensen, 41, was wearing a T-shirt bearing the letter &#34;Q,&#34;</a> a symbol of the QAnon conspiracy theory, when he joined the mob that approached Capitol police officer Eugene Goodman inside the building and followed the officer up two flights of stairs.</p><p>US District Judge Timothy Kelly said deciding whether to free Jensen from jail pending trial was a &#34;close case,&#34; but he ultimately agreed to release the Des Moines resident on house arrest with electronic location monitoring. The judge also barred him from accessing the internet on any electronic devices.</p><p>The judge said Jensen&#39;s actions during his confrontation of Goodman were &#34;deeply concerning and quite serious.&#34; But he noted that Jensen is not accused of toppling any barricades, damaging any property or fighting with anybody at the Capitol.</p><p>&#34;That said, he clearly disobeyed Officer Goodman and other officers, and he did position himself near the front of a mob as he ran up the stairs toward Officer Goodman,&#34; the judge said. &#34;That may be some leadership, but only in the narrowest sense.&#34;</p><p>Kelly noted that a video captured Jensen referring to the Capitol building as the White House. The judge said he didn&#39;t believe that Jensen could have coordinated with others or planned an attack in advance &#34;when he had no basic understanding of where he even was that day.&#34;</p><h2>Lawyers zeroed in on Jensen&#39;s belief in the QAnon conspiracy theory</h2><p>Prosecutors said Jensen is a self-proclaimed &#34;digital soldier&#34; and &#34;religious&#34; adherent of QAnon, the conspiracy theory that has centered on the baseless belief that former President Donald Trump was secretly waging a campaign against a Satan-worshipping, child sex trafficking cabal of &#34;deep state&#34; enemies, Hollywood elites and Democratic foes.</p><p>Jensen traveled to Washington because he was &#34;all about a revolution&#34; and succeeded in his mission to become the &#34;poster boy&#34; for the events at the Capitol that day, prosecutors wrote in court papers. They argued that he poses a danger to the public and must remain jailed.</p><p>Defense attorney Christopher Davis said his client went to the Capitol to observe what QAnon promoters have prophesized as &#34;The Storm,&#34; the day when Trump&#39;s enemies would be rounded up and executed.</p><p>&#34;He was in front of everyone for the now disclosed silly reason to get Q recognized for &#34;The Storm&#34; that was about to take place,&#34; Davis wrote in a court filing.</p><p>Jensen&#39;s lawyer said his client &#34;became a victim of numerous conspiracy theories that were being fed to him over the internet by a number of very clever people, who were uniquely equipped with slight, if any, moral or social consciousness.&#34;</p><p>&#34;Six months later, languishing in a DC Jail cell, locked down most of the time, he feels deceived, recognizing that he bought into a pack of lies,&#34; Davis wrote.</p><p>Jensen faces charges including civil disorder and assaulting, resisting or impeding a law enforcement officer.</p><p>Davis said he tried to book a plane ticket for Jensen but wasn&#39;t able to, leading him to believe that his client is on a no-fly list.</p><p>Few of the more than <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/all-the-us-capitol-pro-trump-riot-arrests-charges-names-2021-1\">500 people charged in the Capitol riot</a> remain locked up while they fight the charges.</p><p>An appeals court ruling in March that led to the release of a mother and son charged in the riot set standards for how judges should weigh whether to keep Jan. 6 defendants locked up awaiting trial.</p><p>The appeals court found that the judge who ordered Eric Munchel and his mother Lisa Eisenhart detained failed to show how they could be a threat to the community, noting that they didn&#39;t assault anyone or destroy anything on Jan. 6.</p><p>Judges have since cited that ruling in several decisions releasing defendants.</p><p>But the appeals court also said last week that people could still be found to be a danger to the public and kept in jail even if they didn&#39;t commit violence on Jan. 6.</p><p>That came in an opinion upholding the pretrial detention of an Army reservist whose <a href=\"https://apnews.com/article/capitol-siege-race-and-ethnicity-ap-top-news-riots-4644edb6f3fa819628760251c846a408\">co-workers told authorities was a known Nazi sympathizer who wore a Hitler mustache</a>. Photo/Evan Vucci, File</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Biden will call voting laws &#39;grounded in autocracy&#39; and &#39;un-American&#39; in a Tuesday address.</li>\n<li>The president&#39;s planned address in Philadelphia is his first major voting rights speech. </li>\n<li>Biden is facing mounting pressure from voting rights activists to take more forceful action. </li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>President Joe Biden will forcefully denounce GOP-backed voting bills as &#34;grounded in autocracy, un-democratic, un-American, and un-patriotic&#34; and make &#34;the moral case&#34; for voting rights in his first major speech on the matter, <a href=\"https://www.politico.com/news/2021/07/13/biden-coalition-voting-rights-499452\">Politico</a> and <a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/2021/07/13/politics/voting-rights-joe-biden-trump-big-lie/index.html\">CNN</a> report. </p><p>Biden will speak at the National Constitution Center in Philadelphia on Tuesday afternoon as the White House and Biden administration<a href=\"https://apnews.com/article/joe-biden-government-and-politics-voting-race-and-ethnicity-voting-rights-7021a19cac8b8a386b77c888b7a24384\"> face mounting pressure</a> to adopt a more forceful stance on voter suppression with his bully pulpit. </p><p>&#34;In the birthplace of American Democracy, President Biden will articulate how to meet the greatest threat to the right to vote and the integrity of our elections since the Civil War, renew his call for vital legislation- to overcome the rash of anti-voter laws motivated by the Big Lie, and underline the all-of-government effort the Biden-Harris Administration launched to use the powers of the executive branch to protect and advance the sacred, constitutional right to vote,&#34; a White House official told CNN. </p><p>Republican lawmakers in 17 states have passed over 28 bills with provisions that tighten voting access as of June 2021, <a href=\"https://www.brennancenter.org/our-work/research-reports/voting-laws-roundup-may-2021\">according to the Brennan Center for Justice</a>, after former President Donald Trump and his allies waged an unprecedented campaign to try to overturn the 2020 election results based on false claims of fraud.  </p><p>And in recent remarks, Biden has also highlighted the growing trend of legislatures also passing provisions that add potential criminal penalties for election officials and give partisan state lawmakers more control over who runs elections and more power to overturn election results. </p><p>Biden will say that &#34;these new insidious moves to empower partisans over independent election authorities in terms of who counts the votes are new and extremely dangerous,&#34; and &#34;are the most significant threat today to the integrity of our elections, and to the security of the right to vote for people of all races and backgrounds,&#34; White House officials told CNN and Politico. </p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong></em><em><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/justice-stephen-breyer-clerks-surprised-retire-supreme-court-seat-biden-2021-7\" data-analytics-position=\"29\" data-analytics-module=\"\">Justice Stephen Breyer&#39;s former clerks want him to retire from the Supreme Court ASAP to open a seat for Biden</a></em></p><p>Biden&#39;s speech also comes as a group of <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/texas-democrats-walking-out-leaving-state-to-block-gop-bills-2021-7\">dozens of Democratic state lawmakers from Texas left the state</a> in droves to deny the quorum necessary to pass election legislation during a special legislative session set to last until August 6. </p><p>Those lawmakers are set to come to Capitol Hill on Tuesday to lobby lawmakers on passing federal legislation to protect voting rights.</p><p>But from the federal level, the White House faces down the problem of a Senate filibuster rule that requires a three-fifths majority for most legislation and no room for error in a Senate split 50-50. </p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/senate-republicans-block-passage-of-democrats-flagship-voting-rights-bill-2021-6\">Republicans in the US Senate filibustered the For The People Act</a>, Democrats&#39; wide-ranging voting rights and democracy reform legislation, on June 22, leaving that bill&#39;s chances dead for now. </p><p>Biden, to the chagrin of many activists, has been unwilling to call for major changes to the Senate filibuster that requires 60 votes to advance to debate on and pass most legislation. </p><p>But White House press secretary Jen Psaki <a href=\"https://www.politico.com/news/2021/07/13/biden-coalition-voting-rights-499452\">told reporters on Monday</a> that the decision over whether to make changes to the filibuster &#34;will be made by members of the Senate, not by this president or any president, frankly, moving forward.&#34; </p><p>&#34;If it were waving a magic wand to get voting rights legislation on his desk through any means, he would do that,&#34; Psaki said. &#34;But it requires the majority of members in the Senate to support changes to the filibuster.&#34;</p><p>Instead, Politico reported, Biden will call for a &#34;new coalition&#34; on voting rights to work at the grassroots level. </p><p>Psaki said Monday that Biden will &#34;continue to lift up, elevate, advocate, engage, [and] empower people across the country,&#34; calling it &#34;the most instructive&#34; thing he can do. </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a src=\"https://i.insider.com/60ed9356ca74780018ae90ab?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Zuck\" height=\"619\" width=\"1238\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Mark Zuckerberg testifies before the House Energy and Commerce January 6, a new book says. </li>\n<li>Executives, it says, mulled asking Mark Zuckerberg to reach out to Trump but decided against it. </li>\n<li>Facebook has long been criticised for allowing page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Facebook was so concerned about the violent rhetoric spreading on its platform ahead of January 6 that it considered contacting President Donald Trump, a new book claims.</p><p>But it instead decided against it for fear of bad publicity, according to an excerpt from &#34;An Ugly Truth&#34; by New York Times reporters Sheera Frenkel and Cecilia Kang.</p><p>The excerpt was published by CNN&#39;s in <a href=\"https://view.newsletters.cnn.com/messages/16261446899794e9adef228db/raw?utm_term=16261446899794e9adef228db&utm_source=cnn_Reliable+Sources+-+July+12%2C+2021&utm_medium=email&utm_campaign=1626144689981&bt_ee=%2FGm0FbBpVRJcvctN6hBkzOXeNmZYs0cACSDSSW%2BhKRWjwjDzL7K0tJDZahQm9gAY&bt_ts=1626144689981;bt_ts=1626144689981\">the July 13 edition of its &#34;Reliable Sources&#34; email</a>.</p><p>It says that security experts at Facebook grew concerned about posts by &#34;domestic extremists&#34; spreading on the platform before January 6, 2021, when Trump had planned a rally near the Capitol to push his bogus election fraud claims. </p><p>Facebook executives, the authors write, &#34;floated getting Zuckerberg to call Trump to find out what the president would say&#34; at the rally.</p><p>&#34;They ultimately decided against the move, out of concern that the conversation would likely leak to the press. It could make Facebook complicit in whatever Trump did that day.&#34;</p><p>In a statement to Insider, a Facebook spokesperson pushed back against the claims though did not address the specific claim that the idea of approaching Trump was dismissed before it was broached with Zuckerberg. </p><p>&#34;No such discussion took place with Mark, nobody suggested he call, and he didn&#39;t. If Trump ignored the pleas of his own Vice President, the idea that Mark Zuckerberg could have influenced him is absurd,&#34; said the spokesperson. </p><p>The anecdote was also related by Bloomberg tech reporter Sarah Frier in <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/07/09/books/review/the-ugly-truth-sheera-frenkel-and-cecilia-kang.html\">a review of the book in The New York Times on Saturday</a>.</p><p>Facebook executives, Frier wrote, decided not to act over the violent rhetoric. &#34;Instead, they sat at home and watched as Trump stirred up the furious crowd, and as threats in Facebook posts escalated into real-world attacks on the Capitol.&#34;</p><p>The book explores Facebook&#39;s failings in allowing extremist propaganda and disinformation to spread on its platforms, reaching millions of its users. The site has long been <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/bleach-miracle-cure-movement-powerful-latin-america-coronavirus-pandemic-2021-5\">accused of acting slowly and in a piecemeal way to counter the spread of extremist content, and lacking a proactive strategy on the issue. </a></p><p>A report by the Tech Transparency Project found that Facebook had <a href=\"https://www.techtransparencyproject.org/articles/capitol-attack-was-months-making-facebook\">been one of the main gathering spaces for the the far-right extremists involved in the Capitol insurrection. </a></p><p>The platform&#39;s CEO, Sheryl Sandberg, last year faced criticism for <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/technology/2021/01/13/facebook-role-in-capitol-protest/\">claiming that the disinformation that fueled the riot was mainly spreading on other platforms</a>.</p><p>The excerpt from the book indicates that top executives knew that this was likely false.</p><p>Facebook in its statement to Insider said that &#34;our teams were vigilant in removing content that violated our policies against inciting violence leading up to January 6th. We were prepared for this and have been more aggressive than any other internet company in combating harmful content, including content that sought to delegitimize the election.&#34;</p><p>The spokesperson pointed to measures including banning extremist movements such as QAnon from the platform, and banning Trump for at least two years for his posts during the riot. </p><p>Trump and Zuckerberg had an uneasy relationship during Trump&#39;s term, with the site one of the Trump campaign&#39;s key platforms for its propaganda efforts.</p><p>Since his ban and departure from office, Trump has<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-to-sue-zuckerberg-dorsey-twitter-facebook-social-media-bans-2021-7\">launched a lawsuit against Facebook and other tech firms</a>, citing his font-family:Arial,sans-serif; font-size:14px; font-style:normal; font-weight:normal; line-height:17px; text-decoration:none; word-wrap:break-word;\" target=\"_blank\"></a></p> <p style=\" color:#c9c8cd; font-family:Arial,sans-serif; font-size:14px; line-height:17px; margin-bottom:0; margin-top:8px; overflow:hidden; padding:8px 0 7px; text-align:center; text-overflow:ellipsis; white-space:nowrap;\">A post shared by Jeff Bezos (@jeffbezos)<time style=\" font-family:Arial,sans-serif; font-size:14px; line-height:17px;\" datetime=\"\"></time>\n\t\t</p></div></blockquote><script async=\"\" defer=\"\" src=\"//platform.instagram.com/en_US/embeds.js\"></script><p>Back in 1961, Funk joined an all-woman space mission dubbed &#34;Mercury 13.&#34; She embarked on an extensive series of tests and trainings, which she aced - she told <a href=\"https://www.texasmonthly.com/articles/wally-funk-couldnt-go-to-space/\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"32047e1b735a6981c2318d035913f7da\">Texas Monthly</a> that the researchers told her she had performed better than any other astronaut in the program, man or woman.</p><p>But the program was ultimately scrapped and Funk never made it to space. In 1962, two of the women from the program testified before the House Committee on Science and Astronautics that they were being denied the opportunity <a href=\"https://www.smithsonianmag.com/history/even-though-i-am-girl-john-glenns-fan-mail-and-sexism-early-space-program-180961443/\">simply because they were women</a>.</p><p>Funk later embarked on a long career in flight, becoming the first female safety inspector at the Federal Aviation Administration and working with the National Transportation and Safety Board, according to Texas Monthly.</p><p>In the video posted to Bezos&#39; Instagram account, Funk said she has now taught over 3,000 people to fly. </p><h2>Blue Origin vs. Virgin Galactic</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60edbbd7ca74780018ae918c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Richard Branson in space aboard a Virgin Galactic rocket plane.\" height=\"900\" width=\"1200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Richard Branson floats in space aboard a Virgin Galactic rocket plane.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Virgin Galactic</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Blue Origin&#39;s New Shepard spacecraft - which was <a href=\"https://www.theverge.com/2021/7/13/22575182/jeff-bezos-blue-origin-launch-space-faa-license-approval\">cleared for takeoff by the FAA</a> on Monday - is scheduled for liftoff at 9 a.m. ET on July 20. </p><p>The flight will take Bezos <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jeff-bezos-blue-origin-first-human-flight-mark-bezos-2021-6\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"a37d89e17345fb5a75411e27e81e94b5\">62 miles above Earth,</a> to the edge of space. Inside the spacecraft, Bezos and his fellow passengers will have three minutes to float around and view Earth from afar or gaze into the depths of outer space.</p><p>While Blue Origin&#39;s mission will be a major milestone - it&#39;s the first time the company has sent human passengers into space - it has since been slightly eclipsed by Virgin Galactic and its billionaire founder, Richard Branson. </p><p>On Sunday, Branson and three crewmates <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/virgin-galactic-rocket-plane-flies-richard-branson-crew-to-space-2021-7\">flew 55 miles above Earth</a> aboard Virgin&#39;s space plane, floated <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/richard-branson-space-flight-virgin-galactic-zero-gravity-photos-unity-2021-7\">in zero gravity</a> for about five minutes, then returned safely to Earth. </p><p>Branson&#39;s flight - which beat Bezos&#39; by nine days, a fact Branson called <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/technology/2021/07/01/branson-bezos-space-race/\">&#34;an incredible, wonderful coincidence&#34;</a> - seemed to rankle Blue Origin, which claimed <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/blue-origin-says-branson-space-flight-wont-count-2021-7\">the flight wouldn&#39;t go high enough to truly count</a>. </p><p>Still, Virgin plans to start offering suborbital flights to space tourists next year, and has already sold 600 tickets to hopeful space tourists, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-virgin-galactic-ticket-richard-branson-space-deposit-price-2021-7\">including SpaceX and Tesla CEO Elon Musk</a> - and, of course, Funk. </p><div
